# Eric Brooks — UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER

*Full-existence intelligence briefing. Independent, evidence-based assessment — the benevolent inverse of total surveillance.*


## Executive Brief (BLUF)

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: ERIC BROOKS, alias "BLADE"
## Executive Brief (BLUF)

---

### Bottom Line, Up Front

The subject is a man who was born inside his own mother's murder and has spent the subsequent century re-staging that moment in a form he can win. Every operationally significant fact in this file — the vocation, the chimerism, the constricted affect, the narrow attachment topography, the daily managed addiction to a substance chemically indistinguishable from his founding trauma, the inability to inhabit a civilian frame for more than hours at a time — resolves to a single structural truth: **Eric Brooks does not have a life that contains vampire-hunting; vampire-hunting is the apparatus by which he is permitted to remain alive at all.** The hunting is not avocation, profession, or even calling in the ordinary sense. It is the load-bearing wall. Remove it and there is no remainder.

This is not a man in crisis. It is a man who organized a crisis, at approximately age nine, into a functional architecture and has maintained that architecture with extraordinary discipline for roughly nine decades. The architecture works. It is also the only thing that works, and he knows this, and he has stopped asking whether anything else could.

---

### The Through-Line

Across fifty years of recorded canon — from the Wolfman/Colan *Tomb of Dracula* origin through the Chichester *Nightstalkers* conversion arc, through the Guggenheim MAX-imprint cold-operator period, through the Cornell MI:13 reluctant-team interval, into the Hill *Blade* ronin register — the surface presentation evolves (quippy to laconic, itinerant to occasionally institutional, monomaniacal to polymathic) but the underlying organization does not move. The same three propositions structure every era:

1. **There exists a category of predator that killed my mother and that the world cannot see clearly.** This proposition is non-negotiable and pre-cognitive; it predates language for him. It generalizes from Frost outward to all vampires, and from vampires outward to all supernatural predation, but it never loses its specific origin charge. Frost remains, after ninety years, the only target that reliably degrades his tactical judgment.

2. **I am the one who can see it, because I was made by it.** The chimerism is not — for him — a curse, a gift, or an identity crisis. It is the operational fact that makes him fit for purpose. He has stopped litigating it. The Morbius-conversion arc and the Switchblade fugue were both narrative tests of whether this proposition could be destabilized; in both cases he returned to baseline with the proposition intact and, if anything, more rigidly held.

3. **Killing the predator is what permits me to be in a relationship with anyone.** This is the proposition installed in the alley with Afari at age nine and never since revised. It is why every intimate he tolerates is either a vampire-adjacent anomaly (Hannibal King, Jacqueline Falsworth) or a caregiver-coded figure he meets in operational context (Faiza Hussain). He has no template for a relationship that does not pass through the hunt first.

The through-line, then, is a recursion: the boy with the broken stake in the alley is still the entire man. Every subsequent operation is a re-enactment with better tools.

---

### The Core Wound and Its Maintenance

The wound is not the mother's death as event. The wound is **the structural fact that he was born into the act of her dying** — that his first action in the world was, biologically, to be present at and constituted by a homicide perpetrated by what would become the category of his life's work. He has no memory of her. He has no memory of not being inside her loss. There is no pre-traumatic baseline self to recover, no childhood Eric who existed before this and could in principle be restored. The wound is constitutive rather than incidental.

This matters because it predicts the maintenance pattern. A wound that *happened to* a person can, in principle, be processed, integrated, mourned, and set down. A wound that *constituted* a person cannot be set down without the person ceasing to exist in any continuous sense. Subject knows this — not in language, but in the body — and has organized his entire defensive structure around **not setting it down** while also **not being destroyed by carrying it**. The compromise is the vocation.

Maintenance operates across four registers, daily and continuously:

- **Somatic maintenance.** The serum dose (or, historically, controlled blood ingestion) is taken on a rigid schedule, with hidden caches at every operational waypoint, and is accompanied by a low-grade continuous shame that the canon has rendered explicit since the *Nightstalkers* run. Every meal is the question. He has answered it the same way every day for decades, which does not make the question stop arriving.

- **Operational maintenance.** Combat, training, weapons preparation, nest reconnaissance, and the polyglot acquisition of occult lore function as the affect-discharge channel that in a normal person would be conversation, grief, or rest. He metabolizes feeling through movement. Idleness is intolerable not because he is restless but because idleness is the condition under which the wound would have to be felt in language, and he does not have language for it.

- **Relational maintenance.** The narrow permitted-intimates set is curated, mostly unconsciously, to consist of figures who mirror his chimerism (a vampire who refuses to feed; a partial vampire) or who supply the caregiving register he lost at birth (Faiza, the surrogate-mothers of his London childhood, Afari before his turning). He leaves these relationships before they can resolve into something that would require him to be a person rather than an operator. The departures from the Harker cell, the Nightstalkers, MI:13, the Mighty Avengers, and the Midnight Sons are not coincidence; they are the same exit, performed serially.

- **Cognitive maintenance.** The threat-assessment default is held in place by the simple expedient of never being off-duty long enough for it to lapse. He has no documented hobby. He has no documented residence in the civilian sense. He has no documented friendships that exist outside an operational frame. The wound is maintained by the structural impossibility of any frame in which it could be metabolized.

The maintenance is, by any clinical standard, expensive. It is also, by any operational standard, successful. He is one of the most effective single-domain combatants in the field, has survived encounters that would have killed any baseline human a hundred times over, and has — in his own terms — kept the line between himself and what he hunts uncrossed for nearly a century. The cost is that there is no Eric who exists outside the line-keeping.

---

### Who He Is at the Deepest Level

Strip the operator surface and what remains is **a child who learned, in a single compressed instant in a London alley, that violence against the right target produces rescue, paternal acceptance, vocation, and the right to be in a room with another person** — and who has been re-enacting that instant, with escalating sophistication and identical underlying structure, ever since. The adult Blade is the apparatus that nine-year-old Eric built to ensure he would never again be in the alley without the broken stake.

He is, beneath the discipline, a man who believes — without ever articulating it — that his existence is conditional on continuous proof of utility against the predator-category. The condition is not imposed from outside; he installed it himself, in the alley, when the alternative was being a powerless child whose mother was eaten by a doctor. He has never revoked it because revoking it would require facing the unprotected child, and the unprotected child is what he has spent ninety years not being.

He is also, beneath the constriction, a man capable of significant tenderness — observed reliably in his protective behavior toward Faiza, in the gravity with which he holds Hannibal King's friendship, in the unspoken courtesies he extends to figures (Quincy Harker, Stephen Strange) whose competence he respects. The tenderness is real. It is simply not available to him in language, only in act, and only at the cost of being framed as professional duty after the fact. He gives what he can give in the only currency he has, which is showing up and standing between.

He is, finally, a man who has made peace with a paradox most people would find unsurvivable: *he is the cure for the disease he carries.* He neither celebrates nor mourns this. He treats it as the operational fact it is. The absence of metaphysical anxiety on this point — visible across every era of the canon — is one of the more remarkable features of the file. He does not ask whether he should exist. He asks only whether the serum supply is adequate and where the next nest is.

---

### Operational Summary

**Capabilities.** Combatant of elite tier, scaled 2–4× human baseline in strength, speed, reflexes, and sensory acuity; accelerated healing; immunity to vampiric conversion; chronological age approaching a century with no significant somatic decline. Edged-weapon specialist (teakwood throwing blades, sword, the signature daywalker blade); proficient in firearms but prefers melee; polyglot; deep occult and folkloric literacy assembled over decades. Operates effectively across geopolitical and mystical strata. Hunts by scent and nocturnal pattern, employing the predator's own mechanics against the predator.

**Vulnerabilities.** Serum dependency with withdrawal symptomatology identical to opioid withdrawal and a homicidal endpoint if untreated; the Thirst as continuous background cognitive load. Frost-coded stimuli reliably degrade tactical judgment. Mother-image stimuli (illusions, suggestions, manipulations) produce disproportionate response. Threat to permitted-intimates produces protective fury beyond rational calculation. Combined-vector failure mode — Frost-adjacent threat to an intimate under conditions of serum scarcity — represents the maximal exploitable configuration; no adversary has yet assembled it in full, though Dracula has approached the perimeter on multiple occasions.

**Behavioral predictability.** High in operational settings, low in relational ones. Will reliably engage threats in his domain, will reliably depart team structures within a predictable interval, will reliably refuse offered help in language while accepting it in act, will reliably exit any frame that requires him to inhabit a civilian self for more than the duration of an immediate operation.

**Failure modes, ranked.** (1) Serum supply interruption sustained beyond his cache redundancy. (2) Loss of a permitted-intimate by his own hand or visible failure to protect. (3) Demonstrated proof that the predator-category cannot be eradicated, i.e., that the founding proposition's implicit goal is structurally impossible — this is the failure mode he has avoided contemplating for a century and which he has no defensive scaffolding against. (4) Forced extended idleness in a non-operational frame, which would compel the wound to be felt in language for which he has no vocabulary.

**Trajectory.** Subject will continue current operational pattern until physiologically or tactically unable. There is no observed evidence of retirement planning, succession planning, or post-vocational self-concept. The closing line of the prior section of this file — *he will do this until he cannot; he has no plan for after* — is the operational summary in its most compressed form. Any benevolent intervention oriented toward understanding rather than redirection should begin from the recognition that the architecture is not a problem to be solved but a survival adaptation to an unrecoverable founding event, and that the appropriate posture is the one Faiza Hussain modeled in MI:13: presence without demand, reframing without insistence, and the patient extension of a category of relationship he does not yet know is available to him.

He is the boy in the alley with the broken stake. He is also the most disciplined adult that boy could have become. Both are true continuously, and the file should be read with both held at once.


## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: ERIC BROOKS, alias "BLADE"
## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

---

### 1.1 The Natal Event (Soho, London)

The subject's life begins inside a homicide. The canonical account, established in *Tomb of Dracula* #13 (Wolfman/Colan, October 1973) and elaborated through Wolfman's *Tomb of Dracula* #s 30, 53, and 58, and again across the *Nightstalkers* (1992–94) recapitulations, the *Blade: Sins of the Father* (Hinz/Platt, 1998) framing pages, and the Bryan Hill *Blade* (2023) cold-open flashbacks, fixes the event with unusual precision for a comics origin. The mother, **Tara Brooks**, a young Black Englishwoman of working-class circumstance, went into obstructed labor in a Soho boarding-house room — variously rendered in art as a single back-room flat off a courtyard, gas-lit, with a wash-basin, a single iron bedstead, and a half-drawn window curtain through which the artist (Colan, then later Platt, then Elena Casagrande in the Hill run) consistently lights the scene by a low oil or gas source. The address is never given a street number in canon; the neighborhood is consistently Soho, consistently within walking distance of a public house and a music hall, consistently described by the surrogate-family figures in flashback as "two streets back of nothing."

The attending physician, called in by another woman in the house when the midwife could not be reached, was **Deacon Frost**. Frost in this period (the original continuity placed the year as 1929; sliding-timeline retellings push the year as late as the early 1970s; the structural facts are stable) was practicing under several aliases as a medical man in immigrant and working-class districts where his predation could be conducted with minimal scrutiny. He arrived with a black leather Gladstone bag and a manner that the surviving women in the house later described, in the recurring flashback motif, as "kind, in the wrong way."

Tara's labor was advanced; she was hemorrhaging. Frost fed on her *during delivery* — the canonical image, repeated by Colan in 1973, Sears in 1998, and Casagrande in 2023, shows Frost's mouth at the throat while the infant crowns. Tara died there. The infant was extracted alive, smeared with both his mother's blood and the contaminating saliva of the predator who had killed her, and carried forward into the room's other women, who took him from Frost without yet understanding what they had seen.

This is the founding fact and the subject can be said, with no metaphorical inflation, to have been **born through his mother's murder.** The vampiric enzymes transferred at the natal moment produced what the *Nightstalkers* and Marc Guggenheim *Blade* (MAX, 2006; Marvel, 2006–07) runs codify as the **dhampir or "daywalker" phenotype**: immunity to vampiric conversion-by-bite, accelerated metabolism, enhanced sensorium, eventual onset of the hemoglobin requirement (the Thirst) in adolescence. He carried this from the first breath. He did not know it for years.

### 1.2 The Father — Absence as Datum

No father is named in the natal accounts. Original Wolfman continuity leaves the paternal slot blank; the implication carried by the surrogate-mother figures across the flashback material is that Tara was unmarried, that the father was either dead, departed, or unacknowledged, and that this circumstance contributed to her being in the back-room boarding house rather than under family care. The Christopher Hinz/Marv Wolfman *Blade: Crescent City Blues* and *Sins of the Father* material declines to fill the slot. The much later **Lucas Cross** retcon (Christopher Hinz, *Blade* vol. 4, 2006) — in which an aged occultist named Lucas Cross is revealed to have been Tara's husband and the subject's biological father, having faked his death and gone underground to fight vampiric cabals — is, as a matter of file-keeping, treated here as a *late-introduced datum that the subject himself did not have access to during the formative period under review.* For the psychology of the child, the father is, throughout childhood and adolescence, an **absence**, not a person. He grew up fatherless and understood himself as fatherless. That the absence was later partly filled by a stranger claiming the slot is a separate event of his adulthood and belongs to a later section of the file.

### 1.3 The Surrogate Mothers (c. Age 0–9)

The infant was raised, in the immediate aftermath of the natal event, by the women of the boarding house — a rotating, informal collective of two to four working-class women, several of whom appear by name in the flashback material (the Wolfman *Tomb of Dracula* recap pages cite a "Madame Vanity," a music-hall figure of indeterminate occupation, as a primary caregiver in the earliest years; later runs add an unnamed laundress and a Jamaican-born seamstress as recurring presences). None of these women possessed independent means. The child was fed, clothed, and lodged out of a pooled domestic economy that the canon depicts as precarious but functional, and that the subject in adulthood references — rarely, and only when pressed — with a flat, protective gratitude.

The granular behavioral inheritances from this period are visible in the adult:

- **A near-allergy to charity framed as charity.** He will accept material aid when it is offered as transactional or as professional courtesy; he refuses it when it is offered as pity. The distinction is one those surrogate mothers would have understood. It was the operational ethic of the house.
- **A specific register of respect toward older Black women** — visible in the MI:13 run with Faiza's mother, visible in the *Tomb of Dracula* run with several minor figures, visible in the Hill *Blade* run in his interactions with a Harlem-based informant. The register is gentler than any other in his repertoire, contains the only "ma'am" he is recorded as using without irony, and does not appear directed at any other demographic.
- **An ease in small, cramped domestic spaces** that is otherwise inconsistent with his hyper-vigilant baseline. He has been depicted across multiple runs occupying single-room safehouses, narrow tenement flats, and back-of-shop quarters with no observable somatic discomfort, while showing visible unease in large, open, "respectable" interiors (penthouses, manors, S.H.I.E.L.D. helicarrier wardrooms). The body was calibrated to one and not the other.

The women told him, from the earliest age at which he could comprehend the story, that his mother had been killed by **"a man with red eyes."** This is the *organizing narrative of his consciousness*. They did not euphemize, did not soften the predator into illness or accident. He grew up knowing, in literal language, that his mother had been murdered by a category of being most people did not believe in. This is not an ordinary childhood epistemology. It produces a child who is, by age five or six, already operating with the **basic cognitive schema of a vampire hunter**: the world contains a hidden predator-class; ordinary people cannot see it; he can. The vocation precedes the training by years.

### 1.4 The Pre-Vocation Child (c. Age 4–9)

What can be reconstructed of the child between the natal event and the encounter with Afari is necessarily inferential, but the canon supplies enough flashback and adult-behavioral residue to populate the picture with high confidence.

**Physical development.** The dhampir physiology was latent but not silent. He would have been a markedly strong, fast, and tireless child by community standards, with sensory acuities that were not yet legible to him as anomalous because he had no baseline of comparison. He would have heard conversations through walls and assumed adults did too. He would have smelled illness, fear, and pregnancy on neighbors without naming what he was smelling. The Hill *Blade* run includes a single panel of the child waking at a sound from three rooms away — this is consistent with the documented adult phenotype and almost certainly reflects the lived sensorium of the boy.

**Schooling.** Formal schooling was minimal and intermittent. He is, as an adult, literate in English with a vocabulary acquired largely through autodidactic reading later in life and through Afari's tutelage. He shows no evidence of having absorbed the cultural canon of an English schoolboy of his nominal period. His arithmetic is operational (tactical, ballistic, dosing) rather than academic. The accent he carries in adulthood — variably rendered across writers but consistently a **deliberately American-inflected register over a substrate of working-class London** — suggests early street English overlaid with conscious later restyling. The substrate is audible only when he is tired, wounded, or speaking to one of the surrogate-mother coded figures.

**Play and proto-aggression.** Flashback material in Wolfman's *Tomb of Dracula* #58 and again in the Andreyko miniseries depicts the boy with a sharpened stick, alone in a courtyard, working out angles of attack against an imagined adversary. Whether this is reconstructive embellishment or a stable canonical datum, it is consistent with the behavioral residue. The adult subject's **grip preferences, footwork, and weapon-deployment idiom** all show signs of being native rather than coached — Afari refined what was already present. The boy was hunting in his head before he had a target.

**Sleep.** Vampiric folklore in his community would have shaped the child's relationship to night. The surrogate mothers would have observed nocturnal precautions — locks, salt, the configuration of windows — and the child would have absorbed these as the ordinary furniture of bedtime. The adult subject's nocturnal alertness, his preference for working in the small hours, his apparent ability to function on minimal sleep, all have roots in a childhood in which **night was the operationally significant period of the day.** He was, from the beginning, a nocturnal organism in a nocturnal house.

**Affect.** The earliest behavioral notes the surrogate-family figures give in flashback describe a "quiet" child, a "watchful" child, a child who "did not cry the way the others did." Whether this reflects post-natal physiological difference, the early absence of a primary attachment figure, or simply the temperamental constitution that would later become legible as the adult's constricted affect, the constancy across the canon is the point: he was **affectively constrained from infancy.** The flatness is not a wound the adult acquired. It is the surface he was born with, over a wound he was born inside.

### 1.5 The Alley (c. Age 9): The Founding Event

The single most-cited childhood moment in the canon, returned to in *Tomb of Dracula* #s 13, 53, and 58, in the *Nightstalkers* origin pages, in *Blade: Sins of the Father*, in the Guggenheim MAX run, and in the Hill 2023 run, is the alley.

The boy, approximately nine years old, was on the street alone after dark — running an errand, or returning from one; the canon varies on the pretext, never on the structural fact. He heard or saw a struggle in an alley off the main thoroughfare. He entered the alley. He found an elderly Black man — **Jamal Afari**, an itinerant American jazz trumpeter then performing in London clubs and, secretly, a working vampire hunter — being attacked by two or three vampires. Afari was losing.

The boy did not run. He picked up a broken length of wood — variously rendered as a piece of fruit crate, a broken broom handle, a fence picket — and drove it into the back of one of the assailants. The wood took. The vampire dusted. The remaining attackers fled or were dispatched by Afari, who, bleeding, looked at the child who had just saved his life and understood, in the same instant, several things at once: that the boy was not afraid of what he had just seen, that he had aimed correctly without instruction, and that the dhampir scent on him was unmistakable to a trained hunter.

This is the **founding event** in the structural sense. Within the compressed space of perhaps ninety seconds, the following installations occurred:

1. **Violence was rewarded with rescue.** The boy's first lethal act produced not punishment but salvation — his own and another's. The synaptic association *act of killing the predator = entry into safety* was laid down in adolescence in a form that has never been overwritten.
2. **Killing the predator produced the first paternal recognition of his life.** Afari, in that alley, looked at him and saw him. The previous nine years of surrogate mothering had given him care; this gave him **acknowledgment from a man**, contingent on the act he had just performed. The contingency is the lever. He has been re-earning that acknowledgment every operational night since.
3. **Vocation, identity, and belonging arrived as a single fused package.** He did not first decide to be a hunter and then find Afari; he did not first find Afari and then learn hunting. The boy who walked out of the alley was already, in latent form, the man the file now documents.

The adult subject does not, in the canonical record, speak about this event in language. He has referred to it obliquely on perhaps a dozen documented occasions across fifty years of publication. He has never narrated it in full to another character. Faiza Hussain, during the MI:13 run, asks him once how he started; he gives her one sentence and changes the subject. The event is sealed.

### 1.6 The Afari Period (c. Age 9 to Late Adolescence)

Afari took the boy in. The arrangement, as depicted in flashback, was informal — Afari had no domestic stability of his own, traveling between London engagements and continental gigs, and the boy traveled with him. This is the period in which:

- **The training began.** Edged weapons first (Afari's preference, and a discipline that mapped onto what the boy had already done with the broken wood); then unarmed combat, in a syncretic style Afari had assembled from his own travels (the canon never gives the style a single name; the adult subject's combat idiom shows traces of boxing, capoeira-adjacent low work, and bladework consistent with several knife traditions). Folklore-mechanics were taught alongside the physical training: the rules of sunlight, garlic, running water, invitation, the variable efficacy of religious objects across cultures and centuries, the catalogue of subspecies and bloodlines, the regional differences in vampiric behavior.
- **The boy was named into the work.** "Blade" as operational alias is canonically attributed to Afari, who used it of the boy first as a nickname for his preferred weapon and then as the working name under which he was introduced to the hunter network. The given name (Eric Brooks) recedes from operational use across this period and never fully returns. The adult subject is "Blade" to nearly everyone he meets; "Eric" is reserved for the smallest number of intimates and, even with them, is rarely deployed.
- **The first stable attachment was permitted to form.** Afari was, for several years, the closest thing to a parent the boy had had. The canon depicts the relationship with restraint — Afari is not sentimentalized; he is shown as competent, demanding, occasionally drinking, devoted to his music as much as to the work — but the bond is unambiguous. The adult subject's continued use of jazz as background ambient (rarely depicted but consistently present in establishing panels of his quarters across multiple runs, and explicit in the Hill 2023 run) is a residue.
- **The hunting began in earnest.** By his early-to-mid teens he was operational, working alongside Afari and, increasingly, independently. The London vampire ecology of the period — Dracula-adjacent cells, freelance predators, the occasional aristocratic nest — provided more than enough work.

This period ends, canonically, with **Afari's turning and the boy's killing of Afari**. The exact age at which this occurred is variable across retellings; the structural fact is invariant. Afari was bitten; Afari converted; the now-young-adult subject staked his foster father. This is the **second founding event**, and it installs the recursive structure that will govern every subsequent intimate relationship in his life: *the people I love become the thing I hunt, and I am the one who must end them.* The first relationship he was permitted to have ended this way. He has been managing the implication ever since.

### 1.7 Earliest Behavioral Patterns — The Ground-Floor Inventory

Synthesizing the childhood material into the behavioral substrate observable in the adult:

- **Hypervigilance as baseline, not as state.** Installed by the surrogate-house nocturnal practices, confirmed by the natural sensorium, locked in by the Afari training. He has never operated from a non-hypervigilant baseline because he has never had one.
- **The predator-screen.** By age five or six the child was already scanning rooms and streets for the category that killed his mother. The adult cannot turn this off. It is not a habit; it is the shape of his attention.
- **Constricted affect as native surface.** Documented from infancy in the surrogate-mother flashback notes; sealed by the Afari loss; never substantially modified. He did not become flat; he was flat, and life confirmed the setting.
- **Vocation as identity, not as occupation.** The fusion at the alley has never been undone. He has no off-duty self because there has never been a pre-duty self to return to.
- **The narrow attachment topology.** Mother absent (dead at the moment of his arrival); father absent (structurally); surrogate mothers plural, provisional, and loved at a distance; first chosen attachment killed and then killed by him. The adult's tolerance for intimacy only with anomalous figures (the non-feeding vampire, the partial vampire, the faith-grounded caregiver) is the only attachment configuration this history permits.
- **Respect calibrated to competence and to the surrogate-mother coded register, indifferent to rank.** The house had no hierarchy of office; it had a hierarchy of who could keep the child fed. The adult applies the same scale to S.H.I.E.L.D. directors, Avengers chairs, and street informants.
- **The dosing relationship to substance, prefigured.** The Thirst onset is canonically adolescent, but the child's relationship to bodily discipline — eating what was available, when it was available, in a house where appetite was a thing to be managed — preceded and shaped how he would later structure the serum regimen. The discipline was there before the addiction it would have to govern.
- **The narrative compression.** He learned early, in the surrogate house, to give the story of his mother's death in one sentence: a man with red eyes. The adult's habit of compressing his autobiography to its smallest sayable form was rehearsed before he could read.

This is the ground floor. Every subsequent structure in the file — the Wolfman-era operational mode, the Frost vendetta, the chimeric self-concept, the Hannibal King attachment, the MI:13 reluctant integration, the modern ronin presentation — is built directly on it. The child in the back-room flat, the boy in the alley with the broken stake, and the man this file documents are continuous in a way that few subjects' files permit. The wound he was born inside is the wound he is still inside. The work that was installed in ninety seconds in an alley around his ninth year is the work he is still performing.

Nothing in what follows surprises this beginning.


## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: ERIC BROOKS, alias "BLADE"
## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

---

The window this section covers runs from approximately age nine — the alley intervention that placed him into Jamal Afari's custody — through approximately age twenty-three or twenty-four, by which point the operational identity is fully formed, the foster father is dead by his hand, the first independent kills are accumulated, and the itinerant-hunter pattern that will define the next several decades is locked in. The compressed chronology of these fourteen or fifteen years is doing more structural work than any other stretch of his life. Everything later is *iteration*. This is the *forging*.

---

### A. The Pre-Afari Floor (Ages 0–9): The Boarding House and What Was Left of the Mother

The years preceding the alley intervention are sparsely documented in the canonical record and were never narrated by the subject himself in any sustained way; the file therefore reconstructs them from the surrogate-caregivers' later testimony as recovered in *Tomb of Dracula* flashback material (Wolfman/Colan, #13, #30, and incidental pages in the Marv Wolfman 1990s returns), with structural inferences supplied where evidence is thin.

The Soho boarding house at which Tara Brooks died was, by all accounts, a women's lodging operated semi-informally by a circle of Black expatriate domestics, dancers, and music-trade workers — the surround that comes with the period's London jazz milieu. The infant was kept by this circle rather than surrendered to municipal care. There is no recorded father; whether Tara was widowed, abandoned, or unmarried is a question the subject never asked aloud in any panel and which the surrogates either did not know or did not tell him. This silence — the *missing father question never put into language* — is itself diagnostic, because it shows the suppression of inquiry as already operational by adolescence.

What the surrogates *did* tell him, and told him early and often, was the story of the man with red eyes who came in a doctor's bag and killed his mother during his birth. This was given to him as fact, not folklore. The household believed it. The story was integrated into his self-understanding before he had the developmental capacity to interrogate it. The structural consequence: he never had the experience most trauma survivors must work through of *learning* that the world contains predators. He arrived at consciousness already knowing.

Material conditions through this stretch were straitened. The file places him barefoot for stretches of his early childhood, intermittently schooled, working small errands by age seven, attached strongly to one or two of the older women in the boarding house in a manner consistent with secure-enough surrogate bonding within a fundamentally unstable frame. The relevant inference: he was not a feral child, and the capacity for attachment was preserved by these women in just enough quantity that, when Afari arrived, there was a substrate for it to seize. Without them there is no Blade — only a damaged boy. With them, there is a damaged boy with a *door*.

He is repeatedly described in later flashback as quiet, watchful, and physically forward — the kind of small child who steps toward a fight rather than away from it. This was not yet courage. It was the absence of a developed flight reflex, because the founding image of his world was that his mother had been unable to flee and that fleeing was therefore not what people in his family did.

---

### B. The Alley (Age ~9): The Founding Image

The intervention against the vampires attacking Jamal Afari is the single most important sixty seconds in the subject's biography. Every later behavior in the file resolves back to this moment, and the file must therefore handle it with the granularity it deserves.

The setting, as established in *Tomb of Dracula* #13 and elaborated in later flashbacks, is a Soho back-alley sometime in the late evening; Afari, an American jazz trumpeter then resident in London and already a working vampire hunter under cover of his music career, is set upon by a small nest — likely three, possibly more depending on which retelling is consulted. The boy is in the alley by accident or near-accident; the canon is inconsistent on whether he was running an errand, following Afari out of pre-existing curiosity, or simply cutting through. The structural fact is that he was alone, unattended, and within fifteen feet of an active vampire attack.

The action he takes is to seize a broken length of crate-wood — the file's first weapon — and drive it through the back of the nearest vampire, killing it. He does not run for help. He does not freeze. He does not strike to wound. He kills, on first attempt, with an improvised stake, at age nine, against a target that towered over him. The fact that he succeeded is partly Frost's gift — the latent dhampir physiology was already producing a child who was strong and fast beyond his apparent build — but the *decision* was his and it was made in under a second.

What this established, in a single compressed moment:

1. **Violence as competence.** He discovered that he could do the thing the adults around him could not.
2. **Violence as rescue.** He saved a man's life. This was the first time he had ever been useful.
3. **Violence as recognition.** Afari, surviving, saw him and *named* him — took him in, named him as one of his kind.
4. **Violence as belonging.** The act of killing produced, instantaneously, the family he had not had.

The wiring this lays down is catastrophic and load-bearing in equal measure. Henceforward, intimacy and lethality are not separable in his nervous system. Every later attachment will be made through the channel of shared combat or shared exposure to the hunted category. He will never form a significant relationship in a civilian frame, because the channel by which significant relationships *first opened* for him was the channel of killing.

He keeps no souvenir of the broken stake. Surrogate-care interview material recovered in flashback indicates that the boarding-house women were informed within hours and that the transfer of custody to Afari was effected within days, with their consent and apparent relief — they had known they could not give him what he was becoming. There is no recorded farewell scene. He simply left, and from that point forward referred to the boarding-house years only obliquely.

---

### C. The Afari Years (Ages ~9–~20): Apprenticeship as Re-Parenting

The decade-plus under Jamal Afari is the longest stable interval in the subject's entire life and the only stretch in which he lived inside a continuous, functional caregiver relationship. Its content, structure, and termination are the templates for everything afterward.

**Domestic frame.** Afari maintained working musician's quarters in London with extended periods on the road through Europe and occasional returns to the United States. The boy traveled with him. He was, accordingly, raised partly in green rooms, partly in rented flats above clubs, partly in trains and ferries, partly in the back rooms of churches and synagogues where Afari was running down a lead. He learned to sleep in any chair, to eat on a schedule that was not his, to pack light, and to disappear into a room's furniture when adult conversation required it. These habits are still observable in the modern operational profile fifty years on: he sits with his back to walls, eats fast, packs in under four minutes, and goes invisible at will in social spaces.

**Training curriculum.** Afari trained him systematically across what would in modern terms be called a five-domain syllabus:

- *Edged weapons.* Knives first — small, then larger, then thrown. The teakwood throwing-blades that become his signature in the *Tomb of Dracula* run are an Afari design, taught from approximately age eleven onward. He drilled blade-draws to the point where the motion became somatic. The signature reverse-grip pull is an Afari mannerism the subject inherited and never modified.
- *Unarmed combat.* A composite of Western boxing (Afari's American background) and what the canon vaguely glosses as "Eastern" forms, supplemented over the years by whatever Afari could buy lessons in from itinerant teachers in the cities they passed through. The subject's modern fighting style retains the bobbing, weight-forward boxer's stance as its base.
- *Folklore-mechanics of vampirism.* This is the curriculum no other teacher could have offered. Afari taught him sunlight, garlic, hawthorn, silver, running water, the threshold rule, the host rule, the various regional variants and their reliability ratings — not as superstition but as field-tested operational knowledge. The subject's modern occult literacy, which he performs as craftsman-knowledge rather than scholarship, was laid down here, in evenings spent reading dog-eared monographs in club dressing rooms.
- *Tradecraft.* How to enter a building unseen, how to follow a target through a crowd, how to disappear, how to lie convincingly to police, how to bribe a hotel clerk, how to read a room for the wrong kind of stillness. This was Afari's most valuable bequest after the curriculum on vampires themselves.
- *The music.* Afari taught him trumpet, with mixed results. The subject is competent rather than gifted; he has not been shown playing in canon for decades, and the abandonment of music is itself diagnostic — it is the only piece of Afari he has set down.

**Affective frame.** Afari was, by all reconstruction, a warm man who used the warmth sparingly. He praised competence rather than presence. He did not embrace easily but did not withhold contact when it was offered. He told the boy he was loved approximately twice in the entire decade together, and both times in the context of an operation that might kill them. The subject absorbed this register completely. It is the register he still uses with the few people he loves.

**The Frost question.** Afari knew the Frost narrative — the boarding-house women had transmitted it intact — and made the central pedagogical decision of the apprenticeship: he did not let the boy hunt Frost. He told him, repeatedly, that Frost was beyond him and would remain so until the training was complete, and that any attempt before then would be the boy's death. The subject obeyed. The obedience is itself remarkable — the full canonical force of the Frost obsession was already present in adolescence, and the discipline that could contain it for a decade is the discipline that organizes the modern personality. It is also the source of the specific guilt-content that surfaces around Frost in the operational years: Afari taught him to wait, Afari is dead, and Frost is *still alive*. The discipline contained the obsession but did not extinguish it, and the gap between the two is where the rage lives.

**Emergent powers.** The dhampir physiology surfaced gradually through adolescence rather than at a single threshold. He was strong and fast as a child; in his teens this slid into clearly superhuman ranges, accompanied by the sensory acuity profile (night vision, olfactory predator-screening, auditory range) that would become his single most useful operational asset. The Thirst did not present in this period — it is a later-onset phenomenon, possibly suppressed by ordinary nutrition during growth, possibly latent until first activated by combat exsanguination exposure in his twenties. The canon is unclear and the file accepts the ambiguity. What is clear is that by approximately age sixteen he was operating, under Afari's supervision, as a co-equal field partner rather than as a student, and that Afari's role had shifted from teacher to spotter and occasional moderator of the younger man's escalating aggression.

He had no schooling outside what Afari provided. He is functionally educated to a high level — well-read in the specific domains the work required, competent in several languages picked up across European tours, mathematically and tactically literate — but holds no credentials and presents as a man who learned everything in rooms rather than classrooms. The performed anti-intellectualism noted in the psychological section is rooted here: he learned from a Black jazzman in postwar Europe, in defiance of every institution that would have credentialed him, and the contempt for credentialing is the residue.

**First kills.** Across the apprenticeship years he accumulates a kill count the file estimates in the low double digits — vampires only, no humans, all in defense of self, Afari, or a third party. The kills are clean, ritualized, and consistent: stake or blade to the heart, decapitation as confirmation when time allowed, body disposal per Afari protocol. He does not develop a taste for it in the pathological sense; he develops a *competence* with it that is indistinguishable from taste to outside observers. This distinction will matter enormously across his later life and is consistently misread by allies and enemies alike.

---

### D. The Turning of Jamal Afari and the Second Founding (Age ~20)

The canonical record places the death of Jamal Afari at approximately the subject's twentieth year, possibly slightly later, depending on which retelling is operative. The event is depicted in flashback rather than in real time, and the file therefore reconstructs the sequence rather than narrating it.

Afari was bitten during an operation against a vampire whose specific identity has been variously named across runs (Dracula himself in some tellings, a Dracula-aligned lieutenant in others; the structural fact persists across the variants). The bite was concealed initially — whether by Afari to protect the boy, or by circumstance, is unclear — and the turning proceeded across hours or days. By the time the subject understood what had happened, Afari was no longer Afari.

The killing, when it came, was at Afari's implicit or explicit request. The canon is consistent that the subject did not murder his foster father in surprise or anger; he killed him because Afari had taught him that this was the work and that it applied without exception, *including to Afari himself.* The blade used was, in at least one telling, a knife Afari had given him.

The psychological consequence of this event cannot be overstated and is the second great forging stroke after the alley.

What it installed:

1. **The recursion rule.** Anyone close to him is at elevated risk of becoming the enemy, and his obligation to kill the enemy does not pause for personal relationship. This rule will be tested across every later intimate attachment — Glory, Safron, the various Nightstalkers, in attenuated form even Hannibal King — and the canon will reliably honor it.
2. **The exhaustion of the father-search.** He had one foster father. He killed him. He has not sought another. Quincy Harker, in the *Tomb of Dracula* years, will be offered the role implicitly and refused it explicitly. No later authority figure — not Strange, not Wisdom, not Fury — has ever been permitted the slot. It is closed.
3. **The crystallization of the vocational self.** With Afari dead and the boarding-house women aged or scattered, no civilian frame remained to him. The work was now the entire content of the life. He did not choose this — the field cleared around him and he was standing where he had been trained to stand.
4. **The unspoken question.** Did Afari let himself be bitten because he was tired? The subject has never asked this aloud and has never been shown thinking it in panel, but the question is structurally present in every later moment when an ally takes a wound that could have been avoided. He watches for it. He has not yet found it.

He did not bury Afari in any documented sense. The body was disposed of per protocol — staked, decapitated, ashes appropriately handled. He kept Afari's trumpet for an unspecified period and is shown, in one flashback panel, having lost or surrendered it by his late twenties. There is no grave he visits. The grief was never given an external object and is, accordingly, still active fifty years later in the form of the operational discipline that *is* the only available continuing tribute.

---

### E. The Wandering Year (Age ~20–~21): The First Solo Interval

The interval between Afari's death and the first documented contact with Quincy Harker's hunting cell is reconstructed sparsely. The file estimates approximately a year, possibly somewhat more, during which the subject operated alone in Britain and Western Europe, accumulating kills, refining technique, and — most importantly — learning what he was when there was no one to perform for.

The behavioral patterns that emerged in this interval and that have persisted unaltered:

- **The route.** He learned to work cities in patterns — entering through a transit hub, taking a cheap room paid in cash for three nights, sweeping the likely nest-locations on foot across the first two evenings, executing on the third, exiting before dawn. This template is still observable in modern operations.
- **The kit.** He stabilized on a load-out — multiple blades, stakes, garlic-derivative compound, silver, holy-water vials, a sidearm carried but rarely used — that has expanded but never fundamentally changed. The teakwood throwing-blades were already canonical by the end of this year.
- **The dress.** He developed the habit of dressing for the work in a register that read as fashionable to civilians and as armored to professionals — the leather coat, the visible-but-not-flashy blade rig, the eyewear that doubled as low-light optic. The aesthetic has updated across decades; the underlying *function* of the costume — be unremarkable to the prey, unmistakable to the few — has not.
- **The silence.** He learned, in this year, to go entire days without speaking aloud, and to operate at full capacity in that condition. This is still observable. He can be in the field for seventy-two hours and produce fewer than fifty words.
- **The first Frost attempt.** The file infers, though the canon does not document explicitly, that he made at least one serious attempt on Frost during this interval and was forced to break off. The Frost-obsession's specific texture in the *Tomb of Dracula* years — the mix of personal rage and tactical caution, the willingness to wait for the right configuration rather than charge — has the signature of a man who has already failed at it once and knows the cost of the next failure.

The wandering year ends with his absorption into the Harker cell, which the next section will treat in full. The relevant note here: by the time Harker meets him, he is *already complete.* The personality, the discipline, the gaps, the wound, the work — all in place. Harker will provide a context, not a formation. The formation is over by approximately his twenty-first year, and the remaining sixty-plus years of recorded existence are the working-out of what was set down in this single compressed adolescence under Afari's hand and in the year alone after Afari was gone.

---

### F. Fallout: What the Formation Cost and What It Bought

The forging produced, by approximately age twenty-one, a man with the following profile, every element of which the rest of the file will document in its mature form:

**Bought.** An operational competence sufficient to survive the next eight decades against opponents who routinely killed his peers. A vocational identity that organized grief and rage into sustained purpose rather than letting them disorganize him. A small, durable internal moral code (do not feed; do not kill humans; do not abandon the vulnerable; finish what Afari started) that has held under pressures that have broken better-resourced men. A sensory and physical inheritance that made the work possible at all. The capacity for narrow, intense, anomaly-mediated attachment that has given him the handful of relationships he has been able to keep.

**Cost.** The civilian self, in its entirety — he has no off-duty mode and no plan for one. The capacity to grieve in language — every loss since Afari has been metabolized somatically and operationally rather than spoken. The capacity to seek a father figure — closed at twenty. The capacity to form ordinary intimate attachments with ordinary humans — foreclosed by the structure that demands his intimates be themselves anomalous. The capacity to *stop* — there is no version of this life that ends in retirement, because the formation did not include any image of a self that exists after the work.

The formation is, in summary, exquisitely well-adapted to the work and catastrophically maladapted to anything else, and the subject has spent his entire adult life ensuring that nothing else is required of him. The achievement is real. The cost is real. The file's view, accumulated across the full longitudinal record, is that he knows both and has decided, with the discipline that has organized every other decision in his life, that the trade was the only one available and that he will not revisit it.

He was nine years old in an alley with a piece of broken wood. He was twenty when he killed the man who taught him. He was twenty-one when he walked into Quincy Harker's parlor already finished. Everything subsequent is a long, careful, lethal coda to those twelve years.


## Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

# CHRONOLOGY III — THE DEFINING MIDDLE PERIOD

*Operational years roughly mid-1960s through the early 2000s in narrative-internal time; publication arc from* Tomb of Dracula *#10 (1973) through the* Nightstalkers *run, the brief Switchblade dissociation, the* Blade: Sins of the Father *and Hinz/Sears period, the* Peter Milligan *one-shots and short runs of the late 1990s, and the Guggenheim MAX series of 2006–2007. This is the section of the file in which the subject is fully formed and visibly aging in pattern without aging in body — the period in which the personality stops being assembled and starts being maintained.*

---

## I. The Harker Cell (mid-1960s through 1979 internal time)

The subject enters this period as a freelancer and ends it as a recognizable, if peripheral, fixture of the European supernatural-counterintelligence ecosystem. The entry point of record is his attachment to the **Quincy Harker cell** — an aging, wheelchair-bound vampire hunter operating out of London with a small standing roster (Rachel van Helsing, Frank Drake, Taj Nital, briefly Hannibal King). The subject's documented behaviors across this affiliation form the longitudinal template that every later team affiliation rehearses with minor variation.

He arrives unannounced, vetted by reputation alone (the Soho and Liverpool nest-clearings of the early 1960s, conducted solo, are referenced obliquely in *Tomb of Dracula* #12 and #30). He accepts Harker's authority not because Harker commands it but because Harker has *demonstrated competence over decades* — this is the first canonical instance of the rank-vs-competence calculation that recurs through every subsequent institutional engagement. He never moves into Harker's residence. He maintains a separate boarding-house room in the Soho area within walking distance of the boarding house in which his mother died — a geographical fact never commented on in dialogue and almost certainly never disclosed to Harker, but legible from the established panel-level locations of his lodgings across the run.

**Operational behaviors during the Harker period.** He insists on solo reconnaissance before team engagements; he carries his teakwood throwing blades in a custom rig under the leather coat (the rig is shown being maintained — sharpening, re-edging, replacement of warped pieces — in at least four panel sequences across the run, always alone, always at night, always with the same sequence: count, inspect, sharpen, holster, count again); he eats apart from the team when possible, in cafés and noodle shops rather than at the Harker house table. He sleeps in clothes. He sleeps with a blade under the pillow. He sleeps four to five hours and rises before dawn for a physical training routine (calisthenics, shadowed knife-work) which he conducts on rooftops or in alley spaces — never in a shared training room, even when one is offered.

**The Dracula vendetta proper** is initiated in this period and becomes the public face of his career. The pursuit of Dracula is, importantly, *not* his primary vendetta — the Frost vendetta is older and more personal — but Dracula is the systemic adversary the Harker cell is organized around, and the subject sublimates the Frost-hunger into the Dracula-hunt as the situational substitute. He confronts Dracula directly on at least nine documented occasions during this affiliation; he loses physically in most of them and survives by the daywalker resilience, learning each time. The repeated encounters teach him a behavioral lesson he will carry: *do not engage the apex predator on his terms; engage on yours.* By the late issues of the Wolfman run he is the only member of the Harker cell who can be left alone in a room with Dracula and trusted to disengage rather than die.

**Hannibal King** enters the orbit in *Tomb of Dracula* #25. The relationship is the single most important interpersonal datum of the middle period. King is a vampire who has spent decades feeding only on animal blood, refusing human prey; he is a former private investigator, verbose, wry, self-loathing in a manner that the subject finds tolerable because it is the inverse mirror of his own constriction. They do not become close in the conventional sense. They become *operationally married* — back-to-back in firefights, predictably synchronized in nest entries, capable of going months without contact and resuming as if no time had passed. The subject permits King physical proximity (shared vehicle interiors, shared safe-houses, shared meals where King watches him eat) that he permits no one else in this period. The structural logic, which he never articulates and probably never consciously formulates, is that King has *chosen* against the predation that Frost embodies — King is living proof that the category is not destiny. To tolerate King is to tolerate the possibility of his own survival.

**Frank Drake** is tolerated but not chosen. **Rachel van Helsing** the subject treats with a brittle, slightly formal courtesy that reads, on close panel-analysis, as the management of a sublimated attraction he will not act on — she is human, she is intimate-adjacent within the team, and his attachment rules forbid both. **Taj Nital**, who does not speak, the subject communicates with more comfortably than with the speaking members; the absence of verbal demand suits him.

**The end of the Harker affiliation** is not a rupture but a fade. After Dracula's apparent destruction in the late Wolfman run, the cell dissolves; the subject does not attend Harker's funeral on the page (or it is not depicted, which in the surveillance-file reading is the same fact). He absorbs the loss in the manner that becomes his signature — by relocating, intensifying training, and accepting a contract in another city within the week.

## II. The Wandering Decade (late 1970s through late 1980s internal time)

Between the dissolution of the Harker cell and the formation of the Nightstalkers, the subject enters what the file must call the **wandering decade** — a period of low canonical visibility but high inferential density. He appears in scattered guest spots (*Doctor Strange*, *Marvel Premiere*, *Marvel Comics Presents* shorts) and in flashback references during later runs. The pattern is itinerant contract work across Europe and the eastern seaboard of North America. He moves on roughly six- to eighteen-month cycles, longer when a serum supply line is stable, shorter when the local vampire population is suppressed or has identified him.

**Lodging profile during the wandering decade** (inferred from the consistency of later depictions and the explicit details given in the Hinz novelization, which Wolfman has acknowledged as broadly compatible): rented rooms above businesses with after-dark closing hours, never ground floor, always with two egress routes, paid in cash four to six weeks at a time. Personal effects fit in a single duffel and a long flat case for blades. A second cache — serum, backup weapons, identification documents in two or three alternate names — is established within twenty-four hours of arrival in any new city, geographically separated from the lodging by at least a mile and never directly accessed in daylight or under observation.

**Romantic episodes during this period** are documented for at least three named figures and implied for several others. The pattern is uniform: short duration (weeks to a few months), terminated by either his departure or her death, in the latter case almost always at the hands of vampires who have identified the connection. The 1981 episode with the woman referenced only as **Glory** in later flashback (Andreyko run) ends with her conversion and his having to destroy her; this is the first repetition of the Afari-pattern in a romantic register and the inflection point at which the subject visibly *codifies* the rule he had until then merely tended toward — *do not let civilians close.* From this point forward the romantic record narrows to anomalies (King-equivalents in the romantic register) and one-night engagements with women he assesses as capable of surviving his world without his protection.

**Skill acquisition during the wandering decade** is substantial. He gains working fluency in French, German, sufficient Romanian to interrogate, conversational Mandarin, and reading-grade Latin and Old English for occult sources. He learns the Indonesian and Filipino blade arts in this period (the *kerambit* and short-stick work visible in later issues is not the original Afari training, which was European-sabre-derived). He establishes working relationships with at least four serum chemists across three continents, deliberately distributing the dependency so that no single source can leverage him. He begins reading occult texts in originals rather than translation, but he reads them late at night, alone, and never carries them on his person — the *appearance* of being only a fighter is maintained as operational cover even with allies.

**Sleep architecture in this period** stabilizes into the pattern that will hold for the rest of his life: four to five hours in two segments, the first immediately before dawn (the safest interval), the second a forty-minute afternoon down-cycle in whatever low-stimulus environment he can engineer. He does not dream on the record. The Hinz novelization gives him a recurring dream of the alley with Afari; whether to take this as canonical detail or interpretive license, the file notes that no on-panel depiction of his dream-content exists.

## III. The Vampirization Crisis and the Nightstalkers (early 1990s internal time)

The **Morbius vampirization event** (*Morbius* and adjacent issues, then carried through *Nightstalkers* #1 onward, Chichester, 1992–1994) is the most significant somatic and identity event of the middle period and arguably of the subject's entire recorded life. He is bitten by Morbius — a "living vampire" of pseudo-scientific origin whose bite is mechanistically anomalous — under circumstances in which the subject's daywalker immunity, normally absolute, is bypassed. He converts. For a window of weeks to months of internal time, he is a vampire in the operational sense: he hungers for human blood, he gains nocturnal weaknesses he had never had, he is briefly capable of being commanded by vampire elders.

The behavioral data from the conversion period is extensive and is the empirical basis for several of the diagnostic statements in the psychiatric workup. He **does not feed on a human**, despite extended opportunity and active temptation, across the entire window. He isolates himself; he attempts suicide by sunlight at least once (Chichester #5, depicted ambiguously and recovered from); he requests restraint from King; he refuses to engage in team operations until the conversion can be reversed. The episode demonstrates that the *moral structure* of the personality is more deeply embedded than the *somatic* structure of identity — when the body became what he hunts, the will did not follow.

The reversal, achieved through occult-medical intervention involving Strange and Crane's serum-line research, restores the daywalker baseline but **does not erase the memory of the appetite.** From the Nightstalkers run forward, the subject knows, in a way he did not previously know, precisely what feeding on a human would feel like as an embodied possibility. This becomes the cognitive substrate of the obsessive intrusion described in the psychiatric workup. He dates his serum-discipline practice from this period; the rigid daily scheduling, the cache redundancy, the willingness to brief allies on restraint protocols — all are post-conversion practices.

**The Nightstalkers proper** — the subject, Hannibal King, and Frank Drake operating as a registered occult-investigation firm out of a brownstone — is his most domesticated period. He lives in a shared building. He shares meals (although not from the same dishes, and not the same substances). He participates in routine business decisions. He hates it. The file reads the entire Nightstalkers experiment as a post-traumatic over-correction following the conversion: having confronted the possibility that he was the monster, he attempts a deliberate experiment in being a *person* — and discovers that the personhood does not fit. The Nightstalkers dissolves through a combination of in-narrative violence (the Zarathos arc, the broader Midnight Sons restructuring) and the subject's increasing operational unilateralism; by the run's end he is again leaving rooms without announcing his exit.

## IV. The Switchblade Dissociation (mid-1990s internal time)

The **Switchblade episode** is the second somatic-and-identity disruption of the middle period and the canonical instance of full dissociative fugue in the record. Under combined supernatural manipulation (Reaper, Mephisto-adjacent forces) and the cognitive aftermath of the conversion, the subject's memory and self-identification are overwritten with a constructed alternate persona — Switchblade, a future-derived assassin with no inhibitions against human killing and no attachment to the Frost vendetta. The dissociation lasts months of internal time. Operationally during this window he commits acts the post-restoration personality finds intolerable, including the killing of human beings whom the subject would, in his stable frame, have spared or extracted.

The restoration is partial — the memories are accessible but held at a depersonalized remove; the subject refers to "what Switchblade did" rather than "what I did," and the file notes this as the only sustained instance in the canon of the subject failing to integrate an action under personal authorship. The behavioral residue is a permanent, sub-threshold suspicion of his own continuity of self — *if it happened once it can happen again* — which manifests in the late-middle period as the practice of leaving coded check-in sequences with King and a handful of others, so that they would be alerted if he were to "go off-pattern." This is the operational scaffolding around a fear he would not name.

## V. The Frost Reckoning and the Sins of the Father Period (late 1990s internal time)

The **Hinz/Sears arc** (*Blade: Sins of the Father*, the prose novel, and the related comics period including the Mackie material) is the period in which the Frost vendetta — sublimated through the Dracula years, deferred through the Nightstalkers crisis, suspended during the Switchblade dissociation — is reactivated as the foreground project. Frost has been absent or low-visibility for years of internal time, and the subject's discovery that Frost is active again produces the most visibly degraded tactical judgment in his entire record. He breaks routines. He travels without establishing cache. He confronts Frost in venues of Frost's choosing. He nearly dies twice.

The arc resolves with a confrontation that does not kill Frost (Frost is durable across the canon, repeatedly returning) but that **breaks the structural primacy of the Frost-hunt in the subject's psychology.** From this period forward, the file observes a measurable cooling of the Frost-affect — Frost remains the personal enemy, but the subject ceases to organize his career around Frost's location. The hunt is generalized; the predator-category, rather than the individual predator, becomes the operational target. This is the transition from a man pursuing his mother's killer to a man permanently at war with the conditions that produced his mother's killer, and it is the closing of the most personally raw chapter of the middle period.

## VI. Tradecraft, Routine, and the Body Across the Middle Period

**Daily routine, stabilized by the late 1990s and persistent thereafter:** dawn-adjacent first sleep, waking with hand on blade, immediate olfactory scan of the room (the predator-screening described in the medical section is so automatic that he does not register doing it), serum dose (small dropper-vials in the Crane-derived era, carried in an inside coat pocket on the off-strong-hand side, with a backup vial in a boot sheath), physical training of forty to sixty minutes (always including blade-form work, almost always solo, in declining order of frequency: rooftop, alley, hotel room, gymnasium), single meal of the day usually mid-afternoon (high-protein, low-volume, eaten quickly and with his back to a wall and a sight-line to every entrance), reconnaissance and intelligence work from late afternoon through evening, operational engagement at night, return to lodging in the hour before dawn, second serum dose, second sleep.

**Personal effects, maintained constant across the middle period:** the leather coat (replaced perhaps a dozen times across the period, always to the same cut and weight); the goggles or wraparound glare-protection (varying in style across decades but functionally constant — the daywalker eyes tolerate sunlight but are uncomfortable in high-glare conditions); the blade rig; a smaller working knife on the belt; a sidearm carried but rarely fired (he prefers blades for the silence and the certainty); the duffel; the flat case; a small leatherbound notebook in which he records nothing personal but maintains operational notes in a private shorthand combining English, military map symbols, and occult sigils.

**Speech patterns across the middle period.** The early-period quippiness (the Wolfman-era American-inflected banter, which scans now as a *performance* of nonchalance rather than a feature of personality) erodes through the wandering decade and is essentially gone by the post-conversion period. The mature middle-period speech profile is short sentences, declarative, present-tense, minimal subordination; humor restricted to dry observation, almost always at his own expense or at the absurdity of a situation, never at an ally's expense. He does not use his own first name in self-reference. He answers to "Blade" without inflection; he answers to "Eric" only from King, and the file infers that the permission is unspoken and absolute.

**Geographical pattern across the middle period.** London remains the gravitational center — he returns to it on cycles of one to three years, always to the same general district, always lodging within walking distance of the boarding-house site. New York becomes the secondary anchor during and after the Nightstalkers period. Working circuits include New Orleans, Marseille, Prague, Hong Kong, Mexico City, and a recurring rotation through smaller European cities (Lyon, Brno, Krakow) where vampire activity is endemic and law-enforcement infrastructure thin enough for him to operate. He avoids the American Southwest in this period (sunlight tolerance does not equal comfort; daywalker physiology runs slightly cool, and prolonged heat is fatiguing). He does not return to the African continent during the middle period despite stated intention; the file reads this as avoidance of an ancestral frame he has chosen not to engage.

## VII. Alliances, Brief Affiliations, and the Pattern of Departure

Across the middle period the subject is, briefly, affiliated with or adjacent to: the Harker cell (covered above), the loose Midnight Sons confederation (Strange, Ghost Rider, Morbius, the Darkhold Redeemers, Werewolf-by-Night), the Nightstalkers proper, an undocumented S.H.I.E.L.D. consultant relationship in the mid-1990s (referenced obliquely in later Guggenheim issues), and several one-off operational marriages with European hunters whose names are recorded in the field but who do not recur.

The **pattern of departure** is consistent enough to constitute a behavioral signature. He does not announce intent to leave; he does not negotiate terms of leaving; he does not refuse future cooperation. He simply, at a moment determined by internal calculus opaque to the team, fails to return from a solo reconnaissance, leaves a note that is operational rather than personal, or vanishes between issues. The next contact, when it comes, comes from him and is treated by him as if no rupture had occurred. The file reads this pattern as the only departure protocol consistent with his attachment substrate — he cannot tolerate the affective weight of a farewell, because a farewell would require acknowledging that the relationship had weight.

He has never, in the canonical record across the middle period, been the one to receive a farewell either. Every relationship of the period ends with his departure or the other party's death.

## VIII. The Closing of the Middle Period

By the end of the Guggenheim MAX run (2007 publication, internal-time situating in the mid-2000s) the subject is recognizably the mature operator who will carry forward into the MI:13 period and the modern era. The Frost vendetta is generalized; the Thirst is managed; the chimerism is integrated as fact rather than crisis; the speech is laconic; the routine is fixed; the attachments are narrowed to King (intermittent), the memory of Afari (private), and the open question of whether he will permit another. The middle period has accomplished what middle periods do — it has transformed the raw material of the formative years into the operational architecture of the rest of the life. Nothing structural remains to be built. What remains is maintenance, the slow accumulation of further losses against an unchanging frame, and the continued postponement of the question he has carried since the alley: *what is this for, after the last vampire.*

He has, the file judges, never seriously entertained the question. He has not needed to. The middle period has confirmed for him, exhaustively, that the last vampire will not arrive in his lifetime, and that the work and the man are the same artifact and will end at the same time.


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: ERIC BROOKS, alias "BLADE"
## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

---

### Preamble: Defining the "Recent" Window

For the purposes of this section, "recent" is bracketed as the operational decade extending from the dissolution of MI:13 as a coherent professional home (circa 2009, following the *Vampire State* arc) through the present moment of file assembly. This is the period during which the subject's mode of existence shifts from *episodic team-affiliated operator* to *itinerant senior practitioner of a craft no one else has practiced for as long*. It is also the period in which the file thickens considerably: the subject is now visible across more registers — political, mystical, geopolitical, paternal — than at any prior point, while paradoxically having fewer fixed relational anchors than he has held since adolescence. The recent record is the record of a man approaching the back half of an open-ended lifespan with no scaffolding for what that means.

---

### Phase A: Post-MI:13 Drift (circa 2010 – 2014)

The closure of the *Vampire State* engagement — Dracula's lunar redoubt, the moon-base assault, the recovery of Spitfire from compromise — left the subject professionally orphaned in a way the earlier departures from the Harker cell and the Nightstalkers had not. MI:13 had been the closest thing in his life to a *workplace*: salaried, structured, with named superiors, regular briefings, a tea kettle. When Cornell's run ended and the team did not survive editorially, the subject was not given the courtesy of a clean exit. He simply ceased to appear in scheduled relation to anyone.

The behavioral record across this stretch is intermittent — guest appearances in *Captain Britain and MI:13* aftermath threads, sporadic Strange-orbit pages, the Whedon-era Avengers tangents already noted — but the *shape* of the drift is consistent. He is observed:

- **Moving through North American and Western European urban corridors** with no fixed residence; safe-house leases under cover names (the file infers at least four: a basement room in Whitechapel kept since the Harker years, a warehouse mezzanine in Long Island City, a one-bedroom in the Marais arrondissement, a converted garage in New Orleans East). None of these is a *home* in the experiential sense; each contains a serum cache, a sleeping pallet, a single chair, a wall map, and an exit.
- **Operating largely solo**, with brief contract-style team-ups (Misty Knight, Iron Fist, sporadic Doctor Strange consultations). He is described in this window by other operators as "available but not present" — meaning that he can be raised when needed and will appear, but does not maintain the lateral chatter that holds a community of operators together.
- **Drinking sparingly and eating sparingly.** The somatic profile in this period tightens; he is leaner in artists' depictions, the cheekbones more pronounced, the standing posture marginally more economical. This is not deprivation. It is the metabolic recalibration of a body whose proprietor has decided he does not need much.

The dominant affective signature of Phase A is *low-grade grief without object.* Spitfire is alive and well; Faiza is alive and well; King is functional. He has not lost anyone. But he has lost a *frame* — the brief experiment of being a salaried Englishman with colleagues — and he is mourning the frame without permitting himself to name it.

---

### Phase B: The Mighty Avengers and the Brief Civic Experiment (circa 2013 – 2015)

His participation in the Al Ewing *Mighty Avengers* / *Captain America and the Mighty Avengers* run is, in the long arc of the file, anomalous and deserves close reading. The team — Luke Cage, Monica Rambeau, Power Man, White Tiger, She-Hulk, Spectrum, Adam Brashear, Kaluu, the subject — was a deliberate civic-scale Avengers, headquartered in Harlem, oriented toward community rather than cosmic engagement. The subject's presence on it has been remarked upon by analysts as surprising.

It is not, on this file's reading, surprising. It is diagnostic.
