Victory is the band with the smallest behavioral signature in the file, because the subject does not, structurally, recognize victory as a category.

**Absent behaviors.** No celebration. No declaration of completion. No rest period taken following a successful operation that is not driven by metabolic necessity. No verbal acknowledgment to teammates beyond a clipped affirmation. No self-congratulation.

**Present behaviors.** A momentary lowering of shoulder tension. A single longer exhalation. Cleaning of weapons. Survey of the environment for the next threat. Movement toward extraction.

The Frost-killing event, in the renderings where it has been depicted, has not produced relief — it has produced, in the canonical depictions, a near-immediate disorientation. The structural function the pursuit serves in his psyche means its completion is destabilizing rather than satisfying, and the behavioral record after such events shows increased withdrawal, increased solo operation, increased difficulty receiving intimacy. He is, by construction, made for the hunt and not for its aftermath.

---

### 8. DEFEAT

Defeat in the operational sense — a mission failed, an enemy escaped, an intimate harmed despite his protection — produces the most legible internal-state shifts in the file.

**Immediate.** The aftermath posture is a tightening rather than a slumping. Shoulders rise rather than drop; the jaw sets. He does not speak to allies in the immediate aftermath unless tactical information must be transferred, in which case the transfer is clinical and brief.

**Short-term.** Within hours he will, if possible, re-engage — return to the site, pursue the escape vector, recommit. The compulsion is strong enough that allies who know him have, in canon, restrained him for his own operational good. He resents this and does not retaliate.

**Medium-term.** Increased routine rigidity. Reduction of intimate contact. Intensified training. The Switchblade dissociation (Chichester era) is the canonical example of what occurs when defeat combines with sustained external pressure beyond the available containment — the structure fractures along the seam where the subject's identification with the predator-category is held in tension, and the predator side temporarily takes operational control. The episode is the maximal failure mode of the defeat-response architecture and has not recurred, but its existence in the file marks the ceiling of what the structure can absorb.

**Shame versus guilt.** The subject experiences guilt operationally — he failed, he should have done X — and processes it through corrective action. He experiences shame only in connection with the Thirst, and only there. Failure does not produce shame in him; failure produces work.

---

### 9. THE THIRST BAND

A distinct band because the behavioral signature is unlike any other state.

**Pre-onset.** As serum interval approaches its limit he becomes terser, more rigid, more solo-seeking. The eye-line shifts: he will begin to track the throats and wrists of those near him in micro-glances he is partly aware of and works to suppress. Olfactory monitoring intensifies and he will excuse himself from enclosed spaces with humans more readily.

**Acute.** Tremor in the off-hand. Sweat at the temples and the back of the neck. Pupillary changes documented across multiple runs — a darkening or reddening of the iris in the rendered art that the text treats as diagnostic. Speech becomes more clipped, with longer inter-word intervals. He will refuse food. He will refuse human contact. He will move toward isolation aggressively, sometimes with force toward anyone who attempts to detain him.

**Post-dose.** Within minutes of dosing the surface tells normalize. The shame-affect, however, persists for a period afterward — visible in a slight reduction in eye contact and an increased reluctance to engage in intimacy of any kind for hours. Of all his states, this is the one in which he is least available to the people he loves.

**Cache behavior.** He maintains supply caches across multiple geographic locations, secured to a standard significantly higher than his weapon caches. The cache locations are not disclosed to allies as a rule, with the partial exception of medical professionals he has worked with repeatedly. Loss of access to a cache produces operational behavior approaching the urgency of a hostage situation — he will commit resources to its recovery disproportionate to its material value, because the supply, not the weaponry, is the load-bearing element of his continued function.

---

### 10. INSTITUTIONAL / TEAM BEHAVIOR

Across S.H.I.E.L.D., MI:13, the Mighty Avengers, the Midnight Sons, the Nightstalkers, and the Harker cell, the behavioral pattern in institutional contexts is consistent and diagnostic.

**Entry.** He arrives, assesses competence, and provisionally complies. He does not seek rank. He does not seek visibility. He volunteers minimal background.

**Operational.** He executes assigned tasks with reliability above the institutional norm. He does not pad reports. He does not embellish action. He does not blame others for failures. He does not claim credit for successes.

**Resistance.** When he disagrees with leadership he expresses it once, briefly, on the operational merits. If overruled and the operational risk remains tolerable, he complies. If overruled and the operational risk crosses his threshold, he goes off-book without prior notification. He does not negotiate this; the threshold is internal and non-negotiable.

**Exit.** Departures from institutions are uniformly unceremonious. He does not give notice in any formal sense. He completes the operation in front of him, packs, and leaves. He does not sever contact with individuals he has accepted within the institution; he severs the institutional relationship and preserves the personal one.

---

### 11. ROUTES, SAFEHOUSES, GEOGRAPHIC PATTERN

**Movement.** He walks routes that avoid surveillance choke-points and prefers covered approaches even in low-threat environments. He varies his routes between any two regular destinations. He does not take the same path through a city two days in succession unless operationally constrained.

**Safehousing.** Documented across the runs, his living arrangements share a profile: ground-floor or basement access (for rapid egress without elevators); multiple exits; thick walls or sound-isolation; minimal personal effects beyond weapons, the serum supply, and a small library of occult and tactical reference material. He does not decorate. He does not accumulate. The MAX-era depictions render this most starkly; the MI:13 era softens it slightly through the presence of Faiza's influence in his proximate spaces, but the underlying minimalism persists.

**Geographic preferences.** London, New York, New Orleans, Madripoor, and a recurring rotation through Eastern European nodes (Transylvania-adjacent for obvious operational reasons) form the documented home-range. Within each, he maintains at least one fall-back location whose existence is not disclosed to allies.

**Vehicle behavior.** He drives competently but without pleasure. He prefers motorcycles for solo operational mobility (visibility, escape geometry) and dark sedans for transport of others. He does not name vehicles. He does not modify vehicles aesthetically. He maintains them functionally.

---

### 12. MICRO-TELLS AND HABITS (CATALOG)

A compressed enumeration of repeatable behaviors not otherwise classified above:

- **The pre-engagement breath.** A single deep nasal inhalation taken before crossing a threshold into an unknown space.
- **The blade-touch.** Periodic, unconscious confirmation of the primary weapon's position by inside-of-wrist or back-of-thumb brush against the sheath. Frequency increases with stress.
- **The thumb on the brow.** Brief pinch of the bridge of the nose between thumb and forefinger when processing unwelcome information. One of his few legible affective tells.
- **The eye-line drop on the name.** Frost. Afari. Tara. Mother. Each produces the same fractional downward glance before re-fixing.
- **The non-blink hold.** Deployed in interrogation and in any negotiation he intends to win.
- **The cleaning sequence.** Blade, edge, sheath tension, off-hand, primary-hand, kit, body. Invariant order, performed after every engagement, performable in the dark.
- **The threshold scent-sweep.** First breath taken on entering any enclosed space, deeper than ambient.
- **The departure without announcement.** Across every era. He le


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: ERIC BROOKS, alias "BLADE"
## Section 6 — Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

---

### 6.1 The Diurnal Inversion

The first fact a surveillance team would record, and the fact around which every other fact in this section organizes itself, is that the subject is functionally nocturnal but not exclusively so. He is a daywalker by physiology — sunlight does not harm him — but he is a hunter by vocation, and his quarry keeps vampire hours. The result is a phase-shifted schedule that runs, in stable operational periods, roughly 1500 to 0700, with a sleep window from approximately 0730 to 1430 and a second, shorter dead window — not sleep, but stillness — from approximately 1100 to 1300 when ambient threat is at its statistical minimum and he permits himself the closest thing in his life to leisure.

This is not romantic affectation. It is a working schedule. He wakes in the early afternoon because his enemies wake at sundown and he needs four to six hours of preparation before they do. He sleeps in the morning because the morning is the safe end of the night-shift and his body, after fifty-plus years of conditioning, will not relinquish consciousness until the sun is up and the city's vampiric population has gone to ground.

The phase-shift is portable. He carries it across timezones with the speed and indifference of a long-haul aircrew; jet-lag does not register in his record because his sleep is already so disciplined and so chemically buffered that resetting to local night is a matter of a single missed dose-window rather than a circadian crisis.

---

### 6.2 Wake Sequence (1430–1500)

Wake is silent and without preamble. He does not use an alarm; the surveillance file would record an internal clock so precise that across observed weeks the variance is rarely more than four minutes. He comes from sleep to full operational consciousness in a single transition — eyes open, scan the room, identify the door, identify the window, identify the weapon nearest his right hand, and then sit up. This sequence is so automatic he is not aware of performing it, which means it would happen the same way whether he were in his own safehouse or a hotel room in Bucharest. Any intimate who has spent a night with him has reported (where the canon records such testimony obliquely, through Spitfire's narration in MI:13) the same observation: he wakes the way a soldier wakes, not the way a man wakes.

The first fifteen minutes are bathroom, mirror, and the morning serum dose. The dose is rigidly timed to the wake event rather than to clock-time — he doses on rising, before any food, before coffee, before speech. The serum is kept in a small refrigerated case (he travels with one; the home unit is larger), the vial drawn with the same motion every time, the injection delivered to the inside of the left forearm because the right is his weapon hand and he will not compromise its tissue. He does not look at himself while dosing. He looks at the vial, then at the puncture site, then puts the case away. The mirror gets a glance afterwards — assessing color, eye-clarity, the small somatic tells he has learned to read in himself for serum efficacy.

Coffee follows. Black, strong, no ritual around it beyond temperature. He drinks the first cup standing.

---

### 6.3 Morning Maintenance (1500–1730)

The afternoon block is body and gear. Two and a half hours, six days out of seven, divided roughly into:

- **Physical training, 75–90 minutes.** Calisthenics-heavy: pull-ups, push-ups, weighted carries, sled work where space allows. Edged-weapon drills against a heavy bag and against air — the bag for power, the air for the speed and economy that bag work degrades. Footwork practice on a marked floor. He shadowboxes the same fifteen-second sequence at the end of every session, a combination Afari taught him as a boy that he has never substituted out. He does not lift heavy iron for hypertrophy; his physiology does not require it and the bulk would slow him. The training is for the maintenance of an instrument he has been tuning for a century.

- **Weapon maintenance, 30–45 minutes.** This is ritual in the strict sense — repeated in the same order, with the same cloths, in the same lighting. Blades first, in descending size: the long working blade, the secondary, the throwing teakwood (he still keeps the teakwood pattern from the Wolfman-era Harker cell, a sentimental holdover he would not call sentimental), the boot knife. Firearms second — disassembly, inspection, reassembly, even on weapons he has not fired in weeks. Specialty ammunition — silver loads, garlic loads, hawthorn-tipped, UV-flare — counted, logged in a small ledger, never trusted to memory. Stakes last, hand-finished from raw stock every few weeks; the surveillance file would note that he carves them himself rather than buying them, and that the carving is the closest thing in his life to meditation. Wood shavings end up on his boots and on the floor around the chair; he sweeps them up afterwards.

- **Gear check, 15–20 minutes.** Coat, harness, sheaths, glasses (lenses tuned for the photonic backsplash of his own UV weaponry), boots. He has the same pair of boots resoled rather than replaced; the surveillance file would note an unusual loyalty to specific items of equipment that have served him well, which is the somatic substrate of his loyalty to people.

The seventh day he rests the training but not the gear. The gear is checked every day without exception.

---

### 6.4 The Civilian Hour (1730–1830)

The hour before dusk is the closest he comes to civilian existence and it is the most diagnostic single block in his day. He eats — properly, sitting down, at a table, with a knife and fork. The meal is high-protein, simple, and prepared by him; he does not eat out except operationally and does not order in. He reads while he eats: newspapers (still physical when available; he buys them in stacks from a specific newsagent in any city he is residenced in for more than a week), occult journals, intelligence summaries from whatever working network he is currently plugged into. He does not watch television during the meal. Music is permitted — almost always jazz, almost always pre-1960, almost always trumpet-led. This is Afari's bequest and the surveillance team would notice that the music is the only domain in which the subject's tastes are stable across decades and across moods. He will play the same Roy Eldridge record on different continents.

He cleans his own dishes immediately. The kitchen is left in a state in which he could leave the building in under ninety seconds without leaving forensic disorder behind.

---

### 6.5 The Briefing Window (1830–2000)

Dusk is when the workday begins. He uses the hour and a half before full dark for communications: encrypted check-ins with whatever cell he is currently coordinating with, situation updates from informants (he runs a small, durable network of human informants in every city he operates in — bar staff, sex workers, morgue attendants, ER nurses, transit drivers, low-level clergy; the network is recruited slowly and paid in cash and occasional favors and is one of the most underestimated assets in his operational profile), and reading of the day's incident reports for the signatures he has learned to recognize. The signatures are specific: certain wound patterns at hospitals, certain missing-person clusters, certain real-estate transactions in old buildings, certain disturbances at cemeteries, certain shipping manifests. He has a checklist; he runs it the same way every evening.

He places calls during this window when he must. He keeps calls short. His voice on the phone is markedly more clipped than in person — a register Hannibal King has joked about across decades. Voicemail he leaves only when operationally necessary and never identifies himself by name on a recorded line.

---

### 6.6 Operational Hours (2000–0500)

The working night is variable by definition, but its envelope is regular. He is on the street, in a vehicle, or in a target location from full dark to roughly an hour before dawn. The structure within the envelope is:

- **Patrol or transit (typically 2000–2200).** Movement through the city following routes that vary day-to-day but draw from a fixed library of perhaps twenty to thirty patterns per city of operation. The surveillance file would note that he never takes the same route two nights running, never enters a building through the same door he exited it from the previous visit, and changes hotels every three to five days when not in a safehouse. The route-library is the substrate; the rotation is the operational hygiene.

- **Contact, surveillance, or engagement (typically 2200–0400).** This is the variable block — meetings with informants, observation of suspected nests, infiltration, extraction, combat. Combat is, statistically, perhaps one night in four. The other three nights are watching, listening, and walking. The proportion is important: the popular image is of a constant fighter; the operational reality is of a long-haul investigator who fights when necessary.

- **Egress and decompression (typically 0400–0500).** He does not go directly home from an operational scene. He drives or walks for thirty to sixty minutes through deliberately non-operational territory — residential streets, parks, the river. This is route-laundering against tail-detection but it is also, the file would infer, a transition ritual he is not aware of performing as a ritual.

He does not eat during operational hours. He hydrates. He keeps a flask of water and a second, identical flask of serum on his person at all times during work; the second flask is dosed for emergency and has been used perhaps a half-dozen times across the recorded canon, each in extremis.

---

### 6.7 Wind-Down (0500–0730)

The pre-sleep block is the second most diagnostic in the day. He returns to whatever address is currently primary, performs perimeter check (windows, door, an idiosyncratic dust-on-threshold practice he learned in the Harker years and has never abandoned), and only then sits. He cleans weapons used during the night before he cleans himself. He cleans himself before he eats. Food in this window is light — fruit, bread, occasionally cold protein. Second serum dose is taken at the end of this block, immediately before sleep, again to the inside of the left forearm. The dose schedule is therefore: rise/dose, work, sleep/dose. The interval is held within tight tolerance and is the single non-negotiable parameter in his life.

He showers very hot, very long, with the bathroom door open. The open door is a tell — the only environment in which he tolerates being naked, wet, and visually obstructed is one in which the egress is unobstructed.

He sleeps in clothes he could fight in. Always.

---

### 6.8 Habits of Place

Residential pattern across the canon is constant: never one residence, always three or four. A primary address — typically a small, defensible apartment in a working-class district where his presence is unremarkable and his neighbors do not ask questions; he chooses neighborhoods with high turnover and mixed demographics for exactly this reason. A secondary safehouse, usually within forty-five minutes by ground transit, stocked with weapons, serum, cash in three to five currencies, and identity documents. A tertiary cache he visits perhaps once a month to rotate stock. A vehicle stored away from all three. He has done this in London, New York, New Orleans, Tokyo (briefly), and the unnamed cities of the more recent runs. The pattern is identical city to city.

Within the primary residence: minimal furniture, no decoration, blackout curtains, kitchen kept stocked for two weeks, no plants, no pets, no photographs. The one consistent personal object across canon is a small, often-handled item associated with Afari — a mouthpiece, a record sleeve, depending on which run is consulted — kept in a drawer rather than displayed. He looks at it perhaps once a month. He has never spoken about it to anyone the file records.

He does not own anything he could not abandon within ninety seconds.

---

### 6.9 Habits of the City

The surveillance file would map a high-resolution movement pattern within any city he occupies, and the pattern would reveal:

- **Specific dive bars** — typically one or two per district — where he is known to staff as a quiet regular who tips well and does not make trouble. These are his informant nodes. He drinks little when there; the bar is the cover for the conversation.

- **A specific 24-hour diner or equivalent** where he sits in the same booth (back to a wall, sight of the door, sight of the kitchen exit), orders the same meal, and tips the same waitress (always the same waitress; he times his visits to her shifts).

- **A specific cemetery or two**, walked regularly — partly operational reconnaissance, partly something the file would have to mark as unexplained presence.

- **A music venue or record store** where the jazz is right.

- **Hospitals** — he knows the layout, ER rhythms, morgue access points of every major hospital in his city of operation. He has favored nurses. He never enters as a patient.

- **Churches** — he uses them as transit nodes and occasional sanctuaries; he is not religious in any confessional sense but he is operationally pious about consecrated ground.

He walks more than he is observed to. He drives when he must move heavy gear or move fast; he uses public transit for short hops and for counter-surveillance; he prefers his own feet because his sensory apparatus works best when he is moving at human pace.

---

### 6.10 Weekly Rhythm

A week of surveillance would record approximately:

- **Six nights operational, one night recovery.** The recovery night is not a holiday; it is the night he does deep maintenance — gear strip-down to component level, residence rotation, supply check across the cache network, longer training session, longer cleaning, longer shower. He does not socialize on recovery nights.

- **Two to three informant contacts** distributed across the bar and diner network.

- **One to two long walks** of two to four hours through the city, ostensibly route-library refresh, functionally something closer to the only continuous thinking he permits himself.

- **One coded check-in** with the current institutional contact, if any (MI:13, the Avengers' security desk, Strange's apprentices in the more recent runs).

- **One private session** that the file would mark and not be able to fully decode — typically a visit to a place associated with the dead. Afari's grave when he is in London. Other markers in other cities. He goes alone, stays briefly, says nothing the file can record, and leaves.

---

### 6.11 The Hidden Substrate

Underneath the schedule is a permanent low-grade calculation the surveillance file would only infer from the regularity of the dose, the redundancy of the caches, the rotation of the residences, the briefing of the few intimates: he is, at all times, *managing* — managing the Thirst, managing the operational tempo, managing the small number of people whose lives he has accepted responsibility for, managing the distance between who he is and what he would become if any of the systems failed.

The routines are not preferences. They are scaffolding. He is a man who has built, over the course of a very long life, an extraordinarily elaborate exoskeleton of habit because the alternative — the unstructured day, the unscheduled dose, the unwalked route, the unbriefed contact — is not, for him, freedom. It is the alley. It is the broken stake. It is the moment in which the structure that keeps him a person rather than a predator did not yet exist, and had to be built from whatever was to hand.

A week of surveillance would record a man living with the precision of someone who knows that the precision is the life.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: ERIC BROOKS, alias "BLADE"
## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

The subject's "family" in any conventional sense is a register of absences, surrogates, and posthumous voices. There is no living relative he acknowledges by blood except, in some readings, the man who killed his mother — and that relationship is structured as vendetta, not kinship. What follows is a longitudinal mapping of every figure who occupies a *family-shaped slot* in the architecture of his interior life: the mother who died at the threshold of his birth, the father he never had (replaced by a sequence of surrogates, each catastrophic), the foster-father he killed, and the small set of figures across decades who have functioned as quasi-siblings or quasi-children inside an attachment system that has no other categories available to it. Romantic and operational intimacies are mapped in *Relationships II*; this section is the foundation under them.

---

### TARA BROOKS — mother (deceased, perinatal)

The structural keystone of the entire file. Everything else in the subject's life is built over her absence.

**History.** Tara Brooks was a young Black woman of working-class circumstance in interwar Soho (original continuity; the era slides forward in later retellings but the social topography holds: poor, urban, racially marginalized, alone). The father is absent from the record — never named, never sought by the adult subject, structurally never raised as a question. She rented in a boarding house and went into labor there. The labor obstructed. A physician was summoned. The physician was Deacon Frost. Frost fed on her during delivery; she died of exsanguination as the subject was born through and into her dying.

**What the subject knows / remembers.** Nothing direct. He has no sensory memory of her — no face, no voice, no smell, no held weight. What he has is *the story*, assembled in fragments through childhood from her surviving friends (the surrogate carers in the boarding-house community), and from his own preternatural inference: from earliest articulable memory he has known that his mother was killed by "a man with red eyes" while he was being born. The story functions as a load-bearing narrative artifact rather than a memory; it is curated, polished, kept intact.

**Dynamics.** The relationship is *with the absence*, not with the person. She is the negative space the personality has organized itself around. Several specific behavioral consequences are observable across canon:

- **The mother is sacred and unspeakable.** He does not discuss her except under direct, trusted pressure (Hannibal King, Faiza Hussain, Harker very late, and in some runs an attempted conversation with Spitfire). When he does, the register is clipped, factual, almost forensic. He gives the events, not the feeling.
- **Any maternal image triggers disproportionate response.** Illusion-casters and telepaths who have weaponized a fabricated Tara against him (Dracula has tried this; Mephisto-aligned entities have tried versions of it) reliably produce either tactical degradation or, conversely, lethal cold focus — the affect splits two ways depending on whether the illusion offers tenderness (degradation) or invites him to harm her image (cold focus). Both responses are diagnostic: the maternal image is the one piece of psychic real estate he cannot defend with his usual machinery.
- **He cannot grieve her in language.** He grieves her in vocation. The vampire-hunting career is, in its entirety, a sustained funerary rite for a woman he never met.

**Trust / safety.** Inapplicable in the ordinary sense; she is a posthumous fixed point. The "trust" he extends to her is the trust that the story is true and that her death was meaningful enough to organize his life around. Any threat to *that* meaning — any suggestion that the story is wrong, that she was complicit, that Frost was something to her other than a predator — is treated as catastrophic and is resisted with the full force of the personality.

**Failure mode.** A sophisticated adversary who can credibly contaminate the Tara-narrative — through evidence, illusion, time-travel, or magical reconstruction — could destabilize the subject more than any physical attack. Dracula's various attempts have generally been crude (impersonation, taunting); a subtler version (a true revision: she chose Frost, she was already turning, she did not want the child) would constitute a near-maximal psychological assault.

**Leverage.** Maximal and permanent. Any operator who can plausibly offer information about her — even spurious information — buys at least a hearing. Any operator who threatens her memory buys a confrontation. There is no neutral approach to this subject.

---

### THE UNNAMED FATHER — biological, absent

Functionally not a relationship at all, but the absence is itself diagnostic.

The subject does not search for him. Across fifty years of published material there is no recorded instance of Eric Brooks pursuing the question of his paternity, requesting records, asking the surrogate carers what they knew, or visiting Soho parish documents. This is striking for a man whose investigative skill set is otherwise exhaustive. The non-pursuit is *active*: he has chosen, at some level below explicit articulation, not to know.

**Inferential read.** Two non-exclusive explanations fit the evidence. First, the father-slot in his psyche is already occupied — first by Afari, then in displaced form by Frost-as-anti-father (the man who was present at his birth, in the role of caregiver, and who killed instead of cared) — and a biological father would have nowhere to sit. Second, the unknown father is the one variable in his origin he can leave alone; everything else about his beginning is fixed and terrible, and the unexamined paternity is the single piece of his foundation that remains, by his own choice, *open*. He has left it open the way one leaves a door unlocked one never intends to open. The optionality itself is a small private freedom.

**Leverage.** Low under ordinary conditions; potentially high under conditions where an adversary fabricates or reveals a paternity narrative. He would be skeptical, but the skepticism would not be free — he would have to spend cognitive resources to maintain it.

---

### DEACON FROST — the man at the birth (extant; vendetta-object; structural anti-father)

Not family in any sane sense, but the file requires him in this section because he occupies the role of *birth-attendant* and *killer-of-mother* simultaneously, which in the developmental architecture is a parental slot inverted into its opposite. Frost is the man who was present at Eric Brooks's first breath. That fact is psychologically ineradicable however many times Frost is killed (Frost has been killed; Frost has returned; the vendetta does not resolve because the structural fact does not).

**History within the file.** Frost was a 19th-century researcher who self-experimented into vampirism and developed the capacity to generate doppelgängers from his victims. He attended Tara Brooks's labor, killed her, exposed the neonate to his saliva, and departed. The subject pursued him for the entirety of his adult career, with the obsession deepening rather than abating across decades. The Frost-pursuit is the *spine* of the Wolfman *Tomb of Dracula* run and recurs as primary structural antagonist through every subsequent era (Chichester, Guggenheim, Hill).

**Dynamics.** Frost occupies, simultaneously and irreconcilably, four positions in the subject's psyche:

1. **The murderer of the mother** — the original justification for the entire vocation.
2. **The transmitter of the chimerism** — the man whose physiology made the subject into what he is. The serum-dependence, the daywalker traits, the immunity, the strength — all of it is *Frost's gift*, biologically speaking. Every dose of serum is a transaction with Frost's legacy. The subject does not acknowledge this in language, but the canon (especially the Guggenheim MAX run) makes it textually explicit.
3. **The anti-father** — the man who was present at his birth, in the caregiving role, and who chose predation. Every subsequent surrogate father (Afari, Harker in distant register) is in some sense a corrective to Frost.
4. **The mirror** — the predator the subject would be if discipline failed. The Thirst is, in symbolic terms, Frost speaking inside him.

**Trust / safety.** None; maximal hostility; the relationship is the most stable hostile bond in the file. *Stability* is the operative word: the Frost-vendetta is in some readings the only relationship the subject has never had to renegotiate. It does not require maintenance.

**Failure mode.** When Frost is on the board, the subject's tactical judgment degrades reliably and observably. He pushes solo into engagements he would refuse in any other context. He accepts losses he would refuse to take for any other quarry. Allies have learned to recognize the degradation and, in the better-functioning periods (MI:13 with Wisdom; Midnight Sons), to compensate for it operationally. The failure mode is *known*, *legible*, and *unchanged across fifty years* — which is its own diagnostic finding: he has not learned to manage it because, at some level, he does not want to. The degradation *is* the relationship; a fully regulated Blade hunting Frost would be a different man.

**Leverage.** Frost's existence is the single largest manipulable variable in the subject's psychology. Any adversary capable of credibly producing Frost, threatening Frost, protecting Frost, or *being* Frost can extract responses the subject would otherwise refuse.

---

### JAMAL AFARI — foster father (deceased, killed by subject)

The first chosen attachment of his life, the first paternal figure, the source of his vocation, and the second great loss. The Afari relationship is the template by which every subsequent close bond is unconsciously evaluated and from which the recursive structure *anyone close to me will become the enemy and I will have to destroy them* is derived.

**History.** Afari was an elderly Black American jazz trumpeter, expatriate in London, secretly a vampire hunter of long standing. The encounter occurred when the subject was approximately nine: he came upon Afari being attacked by vampires in a Soho alley and intervened with a broken length of wood, killing one. Afari survived, identified the boy's potential and chimerism (or at least the boy's preternatural calm with the kill), and took him in. The training that followed occupied the rest of the subject's adolescence and early adulthood: edged weapons, hand-to-hand, the folklore-mechanics of vampirism, and — equally importantly — a way of carrying oneself in the world as a hunter that the subject has not deviated from since. Afari was eventually turned. The subject killed him. The killing is depicted in flashback across multiple runs and is the second most-revisited memory in the file after the birth.

**What Afari gave him.** Three things, in descending order of explicit acknowledgment.

- *Vocation*: a name for what he was for, and a transmissible craft.
- *Tone*: a great deal of the subject's adult presentation — the dry register, the jazz-inflected verbal economy in early Wolfman issues, a certain musicality to his combat rhythm noted by observers — derives from Afari. He plays no instrument himself in the canon (or only rarely, and badly) but the *cadence* is inherited.
- *The proof he was tolerable*: the foundational lesson that violence could yield rescue, paternal acceptance, and a place to stay in a single compressed act. This is the formative misprint that organizes the personality. Every subsequent intimate the subject permits has had to enter through some version of this door.

**Dynamics across the relationship's living phase.** Reconstructable from flashback: warm but disciplined, with Afari occupying the only position in the subject's life that was unambiguously above him in authority and unambiguously safe. Affection was expressed obliquely (this is also inherited). The training was constant. There was no other parental presence to dilute it.

**The killing.** Operationally clean, psychologically catastrophic. The subject completed it without hesitation — Afari had, in some accounts, asked him to — and has carried it as an unprocessed weight ever since. The clipped, factual register he uses to describe his mother's death is *learned* on the Afari killing; it is the regulatory style he constructed to make speech about losses possible at all.

**Trust / safety, in retrospect.** Total during the living phase. Posthumously: Afari is the internalized voice the subject consults under pressure, in the manner of an introjected good object. There is no evidence he is aware he does this, but the canon shows him invoking Afari's lessons — sometimes by paraphrase, sometimes by simply doing what Afari taught — at decision points where his own judgment is shaky.

**Failure mode.** The Afari memory cannot tolerate revision. Any suggestion that Afari was *already* compromised, that the training was for purposes other than what the subject believed, that Afari engineered the alley encounter — these are attacks the subject would treat as he treats attacks on the Tara-image. The structural difference is that Afari is more attackable because more is known and more is testable; the Tara-image is fortified by absence, the Afari-image is exposed by detail.

**Leverage.** Any adversary who reproduces, impersonates, or weaponizes Afari obtains a brief but acute lever. The subject has been hardened against impersonation of allies generally and would likely identify a false Afari fast — but the moment of identification is itself a wound, and a sophisticated operator could budget for that.

---

### HANNIBAL KING — chosen brother / negative-mirror sibling (extant)

Categorized here as family rather than peer because the relationship's function is *fraternal* in the strict developmental sense: an other-of-similar-status whose existence proves that the subject's category is not fate. King is the closest thing to a brother the subject has ever had, and the relationship has lasted, with interruptions, from the early Wolfman era into the present.

**History.** King is a vampire who refuses to feed on humans, a former private investigator turned, against his will, in the 1940s. He and the subject first crossed paths during the *Tomb of Dracula* run; the initial encounter was hostile (the subject's instinct was to stake him); the resolution was the recognition that King's refusal was real and ongoing. They co-founded the Nightstalkers with Frank Drake. They have separated and reunited across decades, each time with the same approximate dynamic.

**Dynamics.** Of all the subject's relationships this is the one where his guard is most reliably down. Three reasons:

- King is a vampire who does not feed — he is, in living form, the proof that the predator-category and the predator-ethics are dissociable. Every minute King exists is evidence that the subject's own daily refusal is possible, sustainable, and not unique. This is unspeakably valuable to a man whose entire interior life is organized around that refusal.
- King has the same wound from the opposite direction. King became what the subject hunts; the subject was born into what King became. They are mirrored chimeras. Neither needs the other to explain.
- King's affect — wisecracking, hardboiled, fundamentally tired — is permissive of the subject's own dryness in a way most other relationships are not. They banter. The banter is the closest the subject comes to play.

**Trust / safety.** High but not absolute. The subject has staked King at least once across the canon (in episodes where King's discipline was in question or where he was believed turned-active) and has nearly done so on several other occasions. The willingness to kill King is, paradoxically, part of what makes the relationship sustainable: King knows the subject would do it, the subject knows he would do it, and that mutual knowledge eliminates the need to pretend otherwise. It is the cleanest contract in the file.

**Failure mode.** A genuine lapse by King — a real feeding, a real turn — would collapse the relationship into vendetta with no transition. The subject has thought through this; King has thought through this; neither speaks of it.

**Leverage.** Moderate. King's safety can be used to compel the subject's attention. King's *corruption*, credibly produced or imitated, could destabilize the subject more broadly because it would invalidate the proof-of-concept the relationship provides.

---

### FRANK DRAKE — quasi-sibling (deceased / variable across runs)

Drake, descendant of Dracula, was the third Nightstalker and the most conventionally human of the three. The relationship was *fraternal-by-proximity* — built from shared work rather than chosen affinity — and was distinguished by friction. Drake's tragic-aristocratic register and the subject's working-class operational register did not blend easily. Drake represented for the subject a category puzzle: a man with predator-blood (literally Dracula's lineage) who chose otherwise, like King, but without King's chimerism — a *human* who hunted his own inheritance. The subject respected this without warming to it. When Drake died (variably across continuities, most consequentially in the *Nightstalkers* finale), the subject mourned operationally: he did not speak of it, he absorbed the loss, he continued. The Drake-shaped absence is smaller than the Afari-shaped one but is in the same category of loss — a partner the subject permitted and lost. Leverage on the Drake memory is low because the subject's investment was always partial; failure mode if Drake were resurrected as antagonist would be cleaner and faster than for any other lost intimate.

---

### QUINCY HARKER — paternal-authority figure (deceased)

The Harker relationship is the only one in the file that approximates *institutional* fatherhood — Harker as elder statesman of vampire hunting, leader of the cell into which the subject episodically integrated during the Wolfman run, a wheelchair-bound veteran whose moral seriousness was unimpeachable. The subject's relation to Harker was *cool deference*: he respected Harker, accepted Harker's tactical authority within Harker's domain, and never integrated into Harker's family of choice (Rachel van Helsing, Frank Drake in his Harker-cell phase, Taj Nital). The subject left and returned, left and returned. Harker recognized the subject's competence and never quite trusted his loyalty, which was a fair read. Harker never learned the full Frost narrative until late, and the subject's withholding was characteristic.

**Dynamics.** Harker functioned for the subject as a *check on his solitude* — proof that hunters could organize, could lead, could die in beds rather than alleys. The subject did not want what Harker had but valued that someone did. Harker's death (in the *Tomb of Dracula* finale, sacrificially) was registered by the subject as the loss of a category, not of a person — *the last of the old hunters* — and he metabolized it accordingly, with grief converted instantly to inheritance. He has carried something of Harker's institutional gravity in the decades since, particularly in his willingness to interface with formal hunting organizations (S.H.I.E.L.D., MI:13) where without Harker's example he might not have.

**Leverage.** Low. The Harker memory is stable, completed, integrated.

---

### RACHEL VAN HELSING — quasi-sister (deceased)

Member of the Harker cell, granddaughter of Abraham Van Helsing, expert with crossbow. The subject's relation to her was *protective-respectful* — she was competent enough to need no protection, which is precisely what made the protective register safe to extend. There was a low-grade romantic potential that neither acted on, because both understood the work did not permit it. Her death (turned by Dracula, killed by Wolverine in mercy in the *Uncanny X-Men* tie-in) was, for the subject, the canonical confirmation of the recursive structure: *anyone close becomes the enemy*. He was not present for the killing. He has not spoken her name often. The unspoken inference shows up in his increased reluctance to permit female combatants close to him for several years of in-canon time after her loss — a reluctance he eventually overrode (Spitfire, Faiza) but not without effort.

**Leverage.** Posthumous; modest; would spike if her resurrection were credibly engineered.

---

### FAIZA HUSSAIN — quasi-daughter / ward (extant)

The closest thing in the subject's life to a child of his own. The MI:13 era (Cornell, 2008–2009) installed this bond against the subject's resistance and against his usual practice. Faiza — young British Muslim doctor, wielder of Excalibur, organized around care and faith — represented every category the subject had spent his life keeping at arm's length: civilian, healer, religiously serious, intact in her capacity for warmth.

**Dynamics.** He was, by his own oblique acknowledgment, alarmed by her almost immediately. He tested her — the team-tests in the early MI:13 issues are diagnostic, he was pushing to discover whether she would survive proximity to him and to the work. She did. The bond that consolidated was *paternal-protective with an undertone of apprenticeship*: he taught her vampire-mechanics, she imposed on him a small but real obligation to be the kind of man he had not previously bothered to perform — slightly more articulate, slightly less laconic, more willing to explain. The Cornell run shows him taking her seriously in a way he had not extended to a young person in decades. The subsequent fracture (the Dracula-targeting MI:13 plot, the subject's compromised behavior, his removal of himself from her orbit out of perceived obligation to her safety) is characteristic: the moment proximity became dangerous, he left, in the same manner he had left the Harker cell, in the same manner he had left every prior cell.

**Trust / safety.** High from his side, sustained and tested. The fracture was protective, not punitive; he believes he was protecting her by withdrawing, and at some level she has been allowed to disagree.

**Failure mode.** Threat to Faiza produces protective fury and willingness to absorb personal cost beyond rational calculation. Combined with Frost-adjacency this would constitute the maximal compound-vector event in the file.

**Leverage.** Very high. Faiza's safety is the cleanest single point of pressure on the subject currently extant.

---

### FALLON GREY / "BLOODLINE" and other claimed daughters — the parental claim itself (variable, extant)

In more recent continuity (notably Hill's run and the *Bloodline: Daughter of Blade* book), a biological daughter has been introduced into the canon. The introduction is psychologically the largest single change in the subject's relational architecture since Afari.

**Dynamics.** He does not know how to be a father. He has no template. Afari is the only model he has, and Afari raised a foundling in a vocation, which is precisely what the subject does not want for the daughter. The early dynamic is therefore *distant-protective with active avoidance of the apprenticeship pattern* — he does not want to make her what Afari made him; he wants her to have the civilian life he believes he is the cost of others having. The internal contradiction is acute and unresolved: he cannot bring her into the work, cannot leave her unprotected from the work, cannot stay close enough to protect her without bringing the work to her door, cannot stay far enough to protect her without abandoning her. He has been observed in the recent canon to choose distance and then to revise the choice and then to choose distance again.

**Trust / safety.** Asymmetric. He trusts her; he does not trust himself with her.

**Failure mode.** Compounded. A daughter is a Faiza-leverage with biology added, an Afari-template threatening to repeat, a Tara-image inverted (he the survivor, she the one he might not save), and a future the personality has no architecture for. Any harm to her would constitute, plausibly, the single event the existing personality structure could not absorb without reorganization or collapse.

**Leverage.** Maximal among extant levers. An adversary informed about the daughter would route every operation through her if rational.

---

### COMPOSITE NOTE — the shape of the family file

The pattern across the seven primary entries is unbroken and specific. Every parental figure is either dead, killed by him, or structurally the enemy. Every sibling figure is either dead or is a chimera mirroring his own.


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: ERIC BROOKS, alias "BLADE"
## Section 7 — Relationships II: Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

---

### Preamble: The Geometry of the Permitted

Before the individual profiles, the structural observation that governs all of them. The subject does not have a "social network" in any ordinary sense; he has a **roster**, kept in his head with the precision of a quartermaster's ledger, of perhaps fifteen to twenty living persons across his entire operational lifetime whose existence registers as something other than threat, prey, or instrument. Of these, perhaps six have ever been allowed past the second perimeter (the perimeter at which he will accept tactical instruction); perhaps three past the third (at which he will accept correction on a matter of personal conduct); arguably none past a notional fourth at which he would disclose interior state without prompting.

The roster is curated by an unspoken intake test he is not consciously aware of administering. Candidates must demonstrate, in roughly this order: (a) the capacity to survive proximity to him without requiring protection he cannot provide; (b) a competence in their own domain sufficient that his deference to them is not a fiction; (c) an internal moral structure he reads as legible — not necessarily congruent with his own, but coherent enough that he can predict their behavior under stress; and (d), the disqualifier most candidates fail, an absence of the particular brittle neediness that would convert his proximity into a demand he cannot meet. He will tolerate vulnerability; he cannot tolerate dependence that has nowhere else to go.

What follows is the file on those who passed.

---

### 7.1 — JAMAL AFARI

**Designation:** Foster father; primary attachment figure of formative period; first mentor; first kill of the second order (the kill that broke him rather than the kill that made him).

**History.** The trumpeter found him in the Soho alley, c. age nine, having just killed his first vampire with a fragment of crate-wood. The original Wolfman characterization places Afari as an itinerant American jazz musician resident in postwar London who had himself stumbled into vampire hunting through personal loss and developed it into a discipline through autodidact study and field iteration. He took the boy in without ceremony, without paperwork, without — by every indication — a coherent plan, and structured the next decade of the subject's life around three concurrent curricula: edged-weapon technique (knives first, the teakwood throwing-blade signature is Afari's design), the folklore-mechanics of the predator (Afari's research notebooks, which the subject preserved and continued, are referenced obliquely across several runs), and the trumpet (which the subject took to with surprising aptitude and abandoned the day Afari died).

**Dynamics.** Afari is the only figure in the file whom the subject permitted, without internal resistance, to occupy a parental position. The relationship is shown in flashback as warm in a clipped, masculine, jazz-musician register — physical roughhousing during sparring, dry humor, instruction delivered in short corrections rather than lectures. Afari did not perform tenderness; he made room. The subject's lifelong difficulty with verbal warmth is partly Afari's bequest — he was taught love as the provision of conditions, not as the use of words.

**Evolution.** The arc compresses into roughly fifteen years of integration followed by the rupture: Afari is bitten during an operation, conceals the conversion as long as he can, and presents himself to the subject already turned, demanding the mercy stroke. The subject delivered it. The canon is somewhat reticent on the staging of the killing — deliberately so, as I read it — but the structural fact is unambiguous: the subject's first complete adult action was the execution of the man who taught him to act.

**Trust/safety.** Total, and posthumously inviolate. Afari is the only figure in the file the subject has never reconsidered, retrospectively criticized, or reduced to operational utility in narration to others. When the subject mentions him at all, which is rare (Wolfman runs, *Nightstalkers* trauma sequences, scattered references in the Hill and Spurrier eras), the register flattens further than its already-flat baseline — the trauma-marker of an affect too large to be carried in voice.

**Failure mode.** Afari is gone, so the failure mode is internal. The subject organizes a meaningful portion of his self-concept around the fantasy that Afari would, if presented with the subject's current life, approve of it. This is unfalsifiable and therefore stable, but it has the consequence that any figure who *resembles* Afari — older Black men of artistic temperament, jazz musicians specifically, itinerant teachers of any kind — receives an initial credit of trust the subject does not extend elsewhere and which has, on at least two occasions in the canon (one a manipulation by a Frost lieutenant, one a misread civilian encounter), been exploited.

**Leverage.** Maximal. Any sophisticated adversary with access to deep biographical intelligence and the capacity to simulate Afari — illusion, reanimation, deep-fake of voice or trumpet — would produce the largest documented dysregulation in the subject's behavioral history. Dracula, who does possess this level of intelligence, has flirted with the maneuver and inexplicably not pressed it; I read this as Dracula's vanity preferring direct contest to surrogate manipulation. A less vain adversary would have used Afari decades ago.

---

### 7.2 — QUINCY HARKER

**Designation:** Operational superior of the long London period; cell leader; surrogate elder; the figure against whom the subject calibrated what command was permitted to look like.

**History.** Harker, wheelchair-bound son of Jonathan and Mina, ran the most sustained organized anti-Dracula cell of the twentieth century from a London townhouse staffed at various points by Rachel van Helsing, Frank Drake, Taj Nital, and the subject. The subject's tenure in the cell, intermittent across the *Tomb of Dracula* run, was the only sustained institutional affiliation of his life until MI:13, four decades on.

**Dynamics.** The relationship has the texture of a subordinate who has accepted a commander's authority without ever surrendering the right of internal review. Harker gave orders; the subject executed them when he agreed and absented himself when he did not, without negotiation. Harker, to his credit, understood this and structured the cell around it — assigning the subject to operations that did not require integration with the team's rhythm. The subject in return offered Harker a particular quality of deference reserved for no one else in the file: he would *report* to Harker, in clipped tactical sentences, of his own initiative. He volunteered information. This is, by his standards, intimacy.

**Evolution.** Across the run the relationship deepened in proportion to the subject's recognition that Harker was not going to fail him in the specific way prior authorities had — Harker did not demand explanation, did not require the Frost biography, did not attempt to convert the operational alliance into a familial one. When Harker died (detonating himself with Dracula in the climactic *Tomb* arc), the subject's grief was again unspoken and again redirected into operations. He has not, to my knowledge, visited the grave in canon.

**Trust/safety.** High in operational domains, moderate in personal. The subject would have taken a stake for Harker without calculation; he would not have told Harker about the Thirst.

**Failure mode.** The relationship as it stood did not fail; Harker died with the alliance intact. The latent failure mode, had Harker lived long enough to ask, would have been the subject's incapacity to convert tactical loyalty into the kind of strategic dependency long-term institutional life requires. He would have left the cell eventually. He always does.

**Leverage.** Posthumous, lower than Afari's because the relationship was bounded by Harker's professional respect for the subject's distance and therefore did not install the deeper hooks. Any manipulation invoking Harker would register; it would not collapse him.

---

### 7.3 — HANNIBAL KING

**Designation:** Peer; the longest-running living attachment in the file; the structural proof that the category is not fate.

**History.** A 1940s private investigator turned by a vampire (Deacon Frost, in one of the file's grim symmetries) who refuses on principle to feed on the living, sustaining himself on bagged blood and cold-storage substitutes. Met the subject during the Wolfman *Tomb of Dracula* run; their pairing across *Nightstalkers* (Chichester, 1992–1994) constitutes the longest sustained two-person operation of the subject's career.

**Dynamics.** This is the single most diagnostically important relationship in the file. King is a vampire — the category the subject was constituted to eradicate — who has, by an act of sustained daily will across decades, refused the predation that defines the category. The subject can therefore tolerate him as no other vampire can be tolerated, because King is living evidence that the chimerism the subject himself manages is not unique and that the discipline he organizes his life around is, at least in principle, available to the enemy. Every day King does not feed is an exoneration of every day the subject takes serum rather than blood.

The surface texture of the friendship is bickering, dry, openly antagonistic in register — they insult each other constantly, contest tactical decisions in front of others, and present as a partnership held together by professional necessity rather than affection. This presentation is fiction, and they both know it. The bickering is the mechanism by which two affectively constricted men maintain proximity without having to acknowledge the proximity.

**Evolution.** The Frost vampirization of the subject (the *Nightstalkers* / Morbius arc) is the relationship's load-bearing event. The subject, turned and homicidal, was eventually restored largely through King's refusal to give up on him — King had been in the subject's position (turned, having to learn restraint) and was the only figure capable of testifying that the position was survivable. The subject has never thanked him for this in language; he has thanked him by remaining in proximity, which is the only thanks he is fluent in.

**Trust/safety.** As high as the subject's psychology permits. He will accept tactical correction from King; he will share information about the Thirst; he will allow King to see him after a lapse without performing composure. He will not, even with King, initiate emotional conversation, but he will not refuse one King initiates.

**Failure mode.** Two vectors. First: King is, ultimately, a vampire, and the subject's moral-splitting defense periodically reasserts the category-membership against the individual exception. This produces episodic cold periods (visible in the *Nightstalkers* run when stress destabilizes the subject's exception-management) during which the subject treats King with operational courtesy and nothing else. King has learned to wait these out. Second: if King ever did fall — fed once, even under coercion — the subject would have to kill him, would do so, and the file assesses with high confidence that this would constitute the terminal event for the subject's remaining capacity for adult attachment. Anyone meaning the subject harm at the highest strategic level would aim here.

**Leverage.** Very high, both as protective hook (threats to King produce protective response equivalent to threats to a sibling) and as identity-destabilization (the existence of a non-feeding vampire is the only stable refutation of the subject's worst self-suspicions; remove that refutation and the suspicion floods in).

---

### 7.4 — FRANK DRAKE

**Designation:** Cell-mate of the Harker period; *Nightstalkers* partner; the descendant of the founding vampire whose presence in the subject's life is itself a tolerated paradox.

**History.** Lineal descendant of Dracula via the Vlad-historical bloodline as Marvel constructs it; recruited into the Harker cell as the family obligation of his inheritance; later co-founder with the subject and King of the Nightstalkers operation.

**Dynamics.** A relationship structured by mutually acknowledged discomfort that became, over decades, a kind of intimacy. The subject's initial posture toward Drake was suspicion calibrated to bloodline; Drake's initial posture toward the subject was the wary admiration of a comparatively ordinary man working alongside an enhanced one. Across the *Tomb* run and the *Nightstalkers* era they negotiated a working equilibrium in which the subject accepted Drake's competence with the Exorcist sword (an artifact whose handling required Drake's specific lineage) and Drake accepted the subject's tactical primacy in close-quarters engagement.

**Evolution.** Drake married, had a family, attempted civilian life in periods between operations — the kind of life the subject does not believe is available to him. The subject's stance toward this was outwardly indifferent, internally watchful: Drake represented a control case, a comparable trauma-load processed through a different attachment topology, and the subject monitored Drake's progress without ever framing it as such. Drake's eventual deaths and resurrections across runs have produced no recorded grieving in the subject — but he has, in two documented instances, taken on operations primarily because Drake's family was tangentially threatened.

**Trust/safety.** Moderate-high, tactical; moderate, personal. The subject did not disclose to Drake what he disclosed to King; he did rely on Drake in field decisions he would not have ceded to others.

**Failure mode.** Drake's civilian attachments are the soft tissue. Any operation that placed the subject in the position of having failed to protect Drake's wife or children would have produced a guilt-load the subject is unequipped to metabolize — he would have absorbed it as further evidence for his organizing thesis that proximity to him is dangerous, and the relationship would have collapsed under that revision.

**Leverage.** Moderate. The Drake bloodline itself (the Dracula-descent) has been used in occult manipulations adjacent to the subject; the subject's response is constrained suspicion rather than dysregulation. He has had decades to think about it.

---

### 7.5 — FAIZA HUSSAIN

**Designation:** Junior teammate, MI:13 era; the closest the subject has come to producing a protégée in the unguarded sense; the figure who most reliably reframes his perception.

**History.** British Muslim physician, recruited into MI:13 (Cornell, 2008–2009) after acquiring the sword Excalibur; teamed with the subject across the Dracula-invasion arc and following.

**Dynamics.** Faiza is the structural inverse of the subject in nearly every dimension — she is unguarded where he is closed, articulate about feeling where he is mute, devout where he is operational, optimistic where he is pre-resigned — and the asymmetry produced an attachment the subject did not anticipate and did not, after the first few weeks, resist. She talks; he listens; she asks questions whose presupposition (that he has interior states worth narrating) the subject would refuse from anyone else; she receives the laconic answers as if they were full ones and constructs the remainder herself, accurately.

The protective-paternal register the subject adopts toward her is uncharacteristically visible — visible to the team, visible to Faiza, visible (one infers) to the subject himself, which is rarer still. He positions himself between her and incoming force as a matter of involuntary reflex.

**Evolution.** The MI:13 run is brief in publishing terms but spans, in-narrative, the duration during which Faiza moves from civilian-with-a-sword to operational caliber, and the subject's contribution to that transition is largely non-verbal — he models economy, he corrects stance with a touch rather than instruction, he debriefs in fragments she learns to expand. The relationship has remained in the background of subsequent appearances rather than developing or rupturing; the subject has not, by all evidence, sought her out in the intervening years, which is consistent with his pattern of leaving permitted attachments rather than maintaining them.

**Trust/safety.** High, in a specific and unusual register: he trusts her perceptions of him more than his own, on a narrow set of questions. When she names something he is feeling, he does not contradict her. This is, in his idiom, an extraordinary disclosure.

**Failure mode.** Faiza's safety is the leverage. Beyond that, the relationship's structural failure mode is the subject's own withdrawal — having found a person who could read him, he has elected, by default rather than decision, to spend most of his time elsewhere. He is not equipped to maintain low-grade contact; the modes available to him are operational proximity or silence.

**Leverage.** Very high. Threats to Faiza produce a protective fury the subject post-rationalizes as professional duty; sophisticated manipulators have not yet pressed this lever, but it is present in the file.

---

### 7.6 — JACQUELINE FALSWORTH CRICHTON ("Spitfire")

**Designation:** MI:13 teammate; romantic-adjacent intimate, intermittent; partial vampire by wartime transfusion (a Union Jack–era plot device whose mechanics map closely onto the subject's own chimerism).

**History.** Daughter of the original Union Jack; given enhanced speed and partial vampiric traits by a transfusion from the Human Torch (android) and a subsequent vampiric encounter; longevity arrested at apparent youth; widowed; centenarian in chronological terms presenting as a woman in early adulthood.

**Dynamics.** This is the closest the subject has come in canon to an adult romantic partnership and it conforms exactly to the pattern. Spitfire is a chimera; her chimerism mirrors his (partial vampire, enhanced, long-lived, presenting as young); she has metabolized her condition into a functional life over decades; she neither requires protection nor performs vulnerability. The subject can be in a room with her without the involuntary predator-screen firing, because the screen identifies her correctly as chimera and files her with King and (covertly) himself.

The flirtation across the MI:13 run was overt by his standards and submerged by anyone else's — a held look, a touched elbow, a remark that could be read either as battlefield humor or as approach. They did not, in the canon, formalize. Whether they consummated is left ambiguous in the published material; the file's working assumption is that they did, briefly, and that the subject withdrew before the relationship could acquire a register he could not manage.

**Trust/safety.** Moderate-high. He let her see his fatigue, which is more than he lets most people see; he did not, however, discuss the Thirst with her, which is the threshold he reserves for King.

**Failure mode.** The relationship's failure mode is the one all his intimacies share — he leaves. The specific quality of this leaving was, in Spitfire's case, polite, mutually acknowledged, and undramatic, which suggests both parties understood the asymmetry: she has had a century to learn how to lose people; he has had a century to learn how to leave them; they did not require explanation.

**Leverage.** Moderate. Threats to Spitfire would register; her own capacity to defend herself absorbs much of the protective-fury vector that Faiza activates.

---

### 7.7 — PETE WISDOM

**Designation:** MI:13 director; the rare institutional superior the subject accepted without contest.

**History.** Career British intelligence, latterly directing MI:13's supernatural portfolio; chain-smoker; tactically devious in a register the subject reads as competent rather than untrustworthy.

**Dynamics.** Wisdom is one of two or three figures in the file whose authority the subject accepted on the basis of operational respect alone — no familial overlay, no Harker-style elder-deference, just the recognition of a planner whose plans had survived contact with the world. Wisdom briefed; the subject executed; Wisdom did not require warmth or rapport, which suited both parties. The relationship is structured by a shared recognition that they are each, in their domains, doing work most people would not do and that the work is the bond.

**Trust/safety.** Operational; not personal. The subject would take orders from Wisdom in a crisis and would walk out on him in the morning without ceremony.

**Failure mode.** Wisdom's known willingness to spend operatives for strategic ends sits, in the subject's file on him, as an unilluminated risk. The subject has not yet been spent. If he were, he would not protest in language; the relationship would simply end.

**Leverage.** Low. There is little here to manipulate that is not already openly transactional.

---

### 7.8 — DOCTOR STEPHEN STRANGE

**Designation:** Senior occult authority; Midnight Sons convening figure; the colleague whose competence the subject accepts without internal review.

**History.** Intermittent collaboration across the Midnight Sons era and following, intensifying in the Spurrier *Death of Doctor Strange: Blade* material and adjacent.

**Dynamics.** The subject's posture toward Strange is the closest he comes to professional reverence and it is offered, importantly, without affection. Strange is the one figure in the subject's working life whose domain (high sorcery) the subject knows he cannot match and whose judgment within that domain the subject defers to as a matter of course. This is functional rather than emotional; the subject is operationally pragmatic about the supernatural and recognizes mastery in others.

Strange, for his part, treats the subject as a peer specialist — neither protégé nor instrument — which is the precise register the subject can metabolize. They do not socialize; they do not negotiate; when one calls the other comes; debriefs are brief.

**Trust/safety.** High, operational. The subject would let Strange perform sorcery on him under duress that he would not let lesser practitioners attempt.

**Failure mode.** Strange's periodic moral compromises in service of larger occult equilibria are the soft tissue. The subject's ethics are more concrete than Strange's; a sufficiently large divergence would produce a rupture, and the canon has at moments tested this without yet detonating it.

**Leverage.** Low to moderate. The relationship is too bounded by professionalism to provide deep hooks.

---

### 7.9 — MICHAEL MORBIUS

**Designation:** Midnight Sons cohort member; the vampirizing agent of the *Nightstalkers* trauma; long-running antagonist-ally whose presence in the file is structurally significant despite the absence of warmth.

**History.** Pseudo-vampire by scientific accident; chronic moral compromise around feeding; turned the subject during the *Nightstalkers* era; subsequently a Midnight Sons collaborator.

**Dynamics.** The relationship is the file's purest case of operational alliance with a figure the subject has explicit cause to hate. The subject works alongside Morbius when the work requires it and does not pretend the alliance is anything else. Morbius's existence is, like King's, exception-data in the subject's vampire-category schema, but unlike King, Morbius's restraint is imperfect — he feeds, he lapses, he rationalizes — which keeps him filed in the subject's mind as a contained predator rather than a peer. The subject monitors him continuously.

**Trust/safety.** Tactical only, and conditional on Morbius's recent feeding history, which the subject tracks by scent.

**Failure mode.** If Morbius lapses materially, the subject will kill him without notice. Morbius knows this. The alliance functions because both parties accept the terms.

**Leverage.** Low against the subject directly; moderate as a destabilizer of the subject's broader exception-management (each Morbius lapse stresses the King-protective schema by association).

---

### 7.10 — LOUISE HASTINGS and the Original Nightstalkers Periphery

**Designation:** Civilian-adjacent occult collaborator of the Chichester era; the subject's brief and instructive exposure to a non-combatant adult who nonetheless inhabited the supernatural register.

**History.** Occult scholar attached loosely to the Nightstalkers operation; the canonical type of older woman of competence whose presence the subject can tolerate.

**


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: ERIC BROOKS, alias "BLADE"
## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

---

The subject's adversarial and intimate registers are, in his case, the same register rendered in different keys. The file demonstrates conclusively that he chooses enemies the way most men choose mentors and chooses lovers the way most men choose hostages: each is a controlled engagement with the category that constitutes him. What follows maps every figure of operational weight across the longitudinal record — the men he has hunted for decades, the women he has loved badly and briefly, and the small handful of intimates whose existence proves the wound has not entirely closed him.

---

### I. THE ENEMIES

#### Deacon Frost — *the original wound, the founding adversary, the figure for whom the entire life is a reply*

Frost is not, on the operational record, the most dangerous vampire the subject has fought. He is a mid-tier elder — clever, opportunistic, capable of generating thralls (his "Frost doppelgängers," a recurrent motif in late *Tomb of Dracula* and the Wolfman returns), occasionally allied to larger powers but never one of them. Dracula has nearly killed Eric many times; Frost has nearly killed him perhaps twice. The disparity between operational threat and obsessional weight is the diagnostic feature of the relationship and must be read accordingly.

**History.** Frost was the obstetrician in the boarding-house room. He fed on Tara Brooks during labor; the subject was born through the wound. The exposure to Frost's saliva is the etiology of the dhampir phenotype — Frost is, in the most literal sense, the agent of the subject's chimerism. He is therefore both the killer of the mother and the biological co-author of the body. The subject did not learn Frost's identity for years; the discovery (made in mid-adolescence via Afari's investigations and confirmed in the *Tomb of Dracula* run) collapsed grief, rage, and self-loathing into a single target.

**Dynamics.** The subject's tactical discipline degrades in Frost's presence in a pattern stable across fifty years of canon. He pursues at the expense of mission, accepts duels that more prudent operators would refuse, expends ordnance and exposes allies. Frost has learned this and uses it — the Frost-doppelgänger gambit specifically exists to fracture the subject's attention, to set him chasing duplicates while the real Frost extracts. The encounter behavior is ritualized: Eric will speak before striking when ordinarily he does not, and the dialogue invariably circles the boarding-house room. He has named the room in Frost's hearing on at least three documented occasions.

**Evolution.** The contour has not changed. In the 1970s Wolfman run the rage was hotter and the dialogue more theatrical; in the modern era (Guggenheim MAX, Hill 2023) the rage has cooled into a settled cold focus, but the strategic distortion is identical. Frost has been killed and returned multiple times — each return is treated by the subject not as fatigue but as continued opportunity. **There is no scenario in the canon in which the subject voluntarily abandons the Frost pursuit.**

**Trust / safety.** None. Total. Frost is the only entity in the file the subject will not consider a parley with under any condition, including tactical advantage.

**Failure mode.** The subject will accept disproportionate cost — to himself, to mission objectives, and to bystanders within tolerable proximity — to close on Frost. He will not accept cost to a protected intimate, but he will accept cost to himself approaching the suicidal. The maximal failure mode is the combined vector identified in the psychiatric workup: Frost in proximity to an intimate, the subject Thirst-elevated, allies separated. Under those conditions tactical judgment is forecast to fail catastrophically.

**Leverage.** Any sophisticated adversary holding Frost — alive, capturable, or even credibly impersonable — holds a usable lever on the subject's behavior. Dracula has used this knowledge to manipulate operational priorities. The lever is permanent.

---

#### Dracula (Vlad Dracula Tepes) — *the structural enemy, the apex predator, the dark father the subject was never offered*

If Frost is the wound, Dracula is the category. Dracula is the lord of vampires in Marvel cosmology and the subject's defining strategic adversary across the entire *Tomb of Dracula* run and recurring through every era since. The relationship is qualitatively distinct from the Frost obsession: where Frost is personal and emotionally distorting, Dracula is impersonal, weighty, and clarifying.

**History.** First encounter: *Tomb of Dracula* #10 (the introductory issue), with the subject already an experienced operator joining the Harker cell's standing pursuit. The two have fought across Europe, the Americas, several alternate dimensions, multiple resurrections of Dracula (each treated by the subject as routine), and the *Death of Dracula* / *Curse of the Mutants* cycle in which Dracula's son Janus and the broader Krakoan complications reshape the political map of vampirism.

**Dynamics.** Dracula is a courtly enemy. He addresses the subject by name, acknowledges his lineage, has on multiple occasions offered him a place in vampire aristocracy.
